Editorial

The International Situation 3

For the sake of the civilization and welfare of all mankind, how can a second world war be appropriate? Analyzing it further from an international perspective: China is currently in the midst of resisting aggression and building the nation, progressing on both fronts. Although the world's state of peace or war will inevitably have a double-edged impact on China, the most urgent task is to defend against aggression and seek survival. All efforts and resources are focused on this, so the world's state of peace or war is naturally regarded as a secondary matter and does not evoke a deep sense of interest. Japan has been invading for years, exhausted and at the end of its rope, with a bleak future and unable to stop. Given this abnormal situation, it may have a unique understanding of the world's peace or war and may even fear that the world will not be in chaos. However, while claiming to be sacred and anti-communist, it sits idly by as the Soviet Union auctions off fishing grounds and does not dare to launch a single arrow, retreating in hesitation. This shows that it does not want to expand the war either. As for Britain and France, they used to compromise and yield to pressure, but the appeasement policy has reached its limit, causing them deep pain and leaving them in a dilemma. However, their subjective intention is still to serve as pillars of peace. The Soviet Union advocates socialism in one country and can calmly observe the situation from a distance, unaffected by the great whirlpool. However, the achievements of the successive five-year plans are only meant to ensure that it is not threatened by violent neighbors. It may wait for the opportunity to watch the fire from across the river, believing that its opportunities will be even better after it has grown stronger, but this is not the case at present. The United States of North America is separated by vast oceans and has a significant influence. The government is cautious, and the opposition party still believes that isolation is the best way to win popular support, which is a sign of its aversion to war. Italy is noisy and impulsive, driven by greed, anger, envy, and hatred. It sharpens its knives and tests them once in Abyssinia and again in Spain. However, its so-called aspirations, which are directed at the Mediterranean, only have a colorful impact through indirect means. It does not have the great courage to fulfill its great desires. Its warriors who have penetrated deep into Spain are still controlled by General Franco and have not crossed the red line. Its warmongering is truly limited to Abyssinia. Germany has cleverly seized and annexed territories without bloodshed, dominating the European continent and creating an unapproachable aura. However, its subjective and objective conditions are not yet ready to become the world's hegemon through a single war. Its annexation of Austria and Czechoslovakia without war should not be taken as clear evidence of its warmongering. As for other countries, they cannot be decisive factors in victory, nor can they rely on their own strength to ensure their own survival. In the event of a major war, it is not guaranteed that they will not be sacrificed as stray bullets, let alone be able to profit from it. Therefore, they sincerely pray for peace. Based on this analysis, it can be said that every country wants international peace and that every person fears and curses war. However, the dynamic evolution of events has reached a point where there is no longer any basis, whether in theory, belief, method, or strength, to give people a glimmer of hope for peace. It seems that the outbreak of a major war is only a matter of time. Mankind claims to be the most intelligent of all beings, but they kill each other uncontrollably. How pitiful! Only five days have passed since Germany's annexation of Czechoslovakia, but the human spirit has suddenly changed. What Germany has done demonstrates that: ambition is insatiable and will continue to progress step by step without end, firstly. Treaty promises and vows are equal to waste paper and nonsense and have no value at all, secondly. The appeasement policy is just a fool's dream, thirdly. These three points have not only deceived and betrayed British Prime Minister Chamberlain, French Prime Minister Daladier, and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, but have also declared the death sentence of international diplomacy with the atrocities of one country. From now on, all languages and words will become useless objects. International relations will only be maintained in two ways: either tolerating atrocities or resisting atrocities. The United States, Britain, and France can no longer remain tolerant and have issued unwavering rebukes one after another. In addition to protesting, Britain and France have recalled their ambassadors to Germany. Britain has discussed abandoning party differences and forming a national unity cabinet. The French parliament has established an authorization law, granting the government great powers to act as it sees fit. The United States has imposed a punitive tax of 25% on German goods, a disguised trade embargo, and has suddenly taken wartime measures for the manufacture of aircraft and the training of air force personnel. These measures cannot be said to necessarily lead to a major war, but they are undoubtedly signs of the eve of a major war. Moreover, Germany's annexation of Czechoslovakia is not enough, and it has made economic demands on Romania, intending to turn the Romanian people into Germany's eternal agricultural slaves. The Romanian government has sought help from Britain, and Poland, Yugoslavia, Bulgaria, Greece, Turkey, and other five countries have expressed their support for Romania as a shield against violence. This is a matter that deserves great attention. Some ethnic Germans living in Eastern and Central Europe have taken the opportunity to demand that their territories be returned to their homeland. It can be seen that Germany's agents are spread everywhere, and any movement can affect the overall situation. This is another matter that deserves great attention. There are rumors that Italy will make demands on France soon. This is another matter that deserves great attention. These three matters are likely to trigger a major war. Every country wants international peace and curses war, as mentioned above, but why is a major war almost imminent? It is the inertia of politics, it is the inertia of mankind. The ambition of ambitious countries is insatiable, they abandon all treaty promises and vows, and they fool the appeasement policy. Germany, Italy, and Japan have been doing this for a long time, not just since the annexation of Czechoslovakia. If they had been contained from the beginning, then maintaining the status quo would have been the inertia. However, they have been tolerated, allowed to act freely, and directly or indirectly rewarded, and as a result, they have become arrogant and extravagant. They have gained more and more, their reliance has grown thicker, and their strength has increased. As a result, they have taken aggressiveness as their inertia, and it is difficult to make them return to a state of rest. Moreover, the "peace first" theory of the past few years has dimmed justice and righteousness, and the weak have been sacrificed. The warmongers have taken aim at peace and flaunted their power and prestige, selling their tactics of coercion and attack. The overall situation is such, and it has a long history. Today, if countries do not resist violence, they can only tolerate it. To effectively resist violence, one must take the initiative to stop it. If the strength is sufficient, one can hope to stop the war with war. If they continue to delay until the disaster is imminent, then they will have gained more, their reliance will have grown thicker, and their strength will have increased. Who will rule the world is unknown.

Japanese Planes Bomb Xiangfan Again 4

Over Two Hundred Bombs Dropped, British Missionary in Pingjiang Already Placed in Coffin

Shashi. At around 3:00 PM on the 18th, eight Japanese planes attacked Shashi in two batches, three planes in one batch and five planes in the other. After circling the city twice, they flew into the airspace above Jiangling, dropping 25 bombs, killing and wounding over 50 civilians, and destroying over 50 civilian houses. The American Church of Christ, the Methodist Church, was also hit by three bombs, killing three people. (18th Telegram)

Nanyang. At 9:30 AM on the 18th, 13 Japanese planes entered the airspace above Xuchang in two batches, dropping two or three dozen bombs, destroying dozens of houses. The residents had already evacuated, so there were not many casualties. Yicheng and other places in northern Hubei were also bombed, details to be investigated. (18th Telegram)

Xiangyang. Xiangfan has been bombed by Japanese planes for three consecutive days, especially severely today. At around 12:00 noon, nine Japanese planes, three of which bombed Xiangyang and six of which bombed Fancheng. At 1:30 PM and 3:30 PM, six Japanese planes repeatedly bombed the area in relays, dropping a total of over two hundred bombs. Fortunately, the residents had already been evacuated, so there were only over twenty casualties. (19th Telegram)

(Chongqing) Chinese troops near Fancheng shot down a Japanese plane. Japanese planes attacked Xiangyang, a Chinese military base in central China, as well as Zhengzhou, a key point connecting the Longhai and Pinghan railways. (19th Huitong Telegram)

(Changsha) The British missionary Li Xiebong, who was killed by Japanese planes in Pingjiang, was the head of the Pingjiang Union District of the Hunan Diocese of the Methodist Church. He was only 35 years old, graduated from the London Methodist Theological Seminary, came to China in 1931, returned to London once in 1937, and came to China again in January of this year. Li was praised by the locals for his administration of the Pingjiang church. When Japanese planes attacked Pingjiang on the 15th, Li was taking refuge in an air-raid shelter next to Qinren School with Pastor Gao Keli and his servant's family of seven. The shelter was hit by a bomb, killing Li and his servant's entire family. Pastor Gao escaped from the rubble and was slightly injured. Pastor Baker Fang, the head of the Hunan Diocese of the Methodist Church, rushed to Pingjiang from Changsha on the morning of the 17th after hearing the bad news to take care of the aftermath for Li. He returned to Changsha that evening. The reporter visited him and learned that Li's body had been dug out from the collapsed air-raid shelter. The condition was terrible and he will be buried in Pingjiang. Pastor Baker also said that Pingjiang had been attacked by Japanese planes 27 times as of the 15th. Because the county is an undefended city, the Japanese planes flew low over the city to observe and drop bombs each time. The Pumou Hospital and Peiren School, which are run by the Methodist Church, are connected to the pastor's residence and occupy a large area in Xiguan, Pingjiang. The rooftops are marked with British flags and have huge British flags hanging on them. It is believed that the Japanese pilots must have known that this was the location of the British charitable organization during the 27 attacks. However, they dropped four large bombs, which makes us feel resentful. The British in Hunan have urgently telegraphed the British Embassy in China to report Li's death in the Japanese bombing, and have also telegraphed his wife in London and his four-year-old daughter to report the bereavement. (17th Telegram)

Lianxian. Nine Japanese planes attacked Sihui at 9:40 AM on the 19th, dropping over 30 bombs on the county seat and its suburbs, destroying dozens of houses and killing and wounding over ten civilians. (19th Telegram)

Japan Plans to Control Chinese Shipping

Raising Public Bonds to Build New Ships

(Tokyo) "Continued Sale News" reports that the National Policy Shipping Federation, organized by the Japanese Ministry of Communications to control Chinese shipping, is scheduled to open on April 1. It is expected that the president of Osaka Merchant Shipping Co., Ltd., Murata, will be appointed as the chairman of the board of directors of the Federation, and the vice president of Nippon Yusen Kaisha, Shimizu, may be appointed as the permanent chairman of the Federation. (18th Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) According to a statement by the Japanese Ministry of Communications, public bonds for the construction of new ships in this fiscal year will reach 90 million Japanese yen, with an annual interest rate of 3.7%. According to the past Japanese shipbuilding financial system, ships built with public bonds were limited to over 4,000 tons each. Now, according to the new regulations, new ships of over 1,000 tons will be built with public bonds. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Former Confidential Secretary to Prince Demchugdongrub, Qi Peizhang, Arrives in Chongqing 5

Qi Exposes Japanese Conspiracy to Drugging Mongolians, Predicts Prince De Will Soon Revolt

(Chongqing) Qi Peizhang (transliteration), a young Mongolian nobleman aged 28, was sent to Tokyo for studies by Prince Demchugdongrub in 1934. He was recalled at the end of last year to serve as Prince De's confidential secretary. Although Qi studied in Japan, he is an anti-Japanese activist. He recently crossed the western part of Suiyuan, overcoming many dangers to reach Chongqing. He reported the situation in Inner Mongolia to the National Government. According to his statement to the Associated Press, he "eloped" after serving as a confidential secretary to the "Mongolian United Autonomous Government" for 28 days. He said that the Japanese are currently intensifying the training of young people in Inner Mongolia under the principle of "Asia for Asians". They claim that the Mongolian and Japanese people share the same origin thousands of years ago. Therefore, the Japanese established a "Mongolian College" in Guihua and "Youth Schools" in Zhangjiakou and Baotou, intending to drug the Inner Mongolian youth and make them pro-Japanese. In addition, the Japanese are also encouraging opium smoking and prostitution in Inner Mongolia. Qi said that Prince De has always been regarded as a traitor, but "he is not so bad as all that." Under Japanese surveillance, Prince De appears to be in great pain. The Japanese garrison in Inner Mongolia consists of only one division, while the Mongolian army under Prince De has nine divisions. They are supplied by the Japanese Kwantung Army from the Northeast, like parasites of the Kwantung Army. The Mongolian army is under strict surveillance by the Japanese army, so it has no heavy artillery. Qi predicted that Prince De would soon revolt. When he left Prince De's headquarters at the end of January, he learned that the Japanese were rushing to build fortifications at various passes between Inner and Outer Mongolia to prevent invasion from Outer Mongolia. (American Associated Press dispatch, 19th)

Yunnan Economic Commission

Controls Trade

(Kunming) In order to control Yunnan's import and export trade, the Yunnan Provincial Economic Commission has established an Import and Export Trade Commission, which is now organized and will begin controlling trade on April 1st. Its scope is limited to several items such as cow and sheepskins, pig bristles, puer tea, and tung oil. The commission currently has offices in Kunming, Gejiu, Bisezhai, Zhaihe and other places. (Dispatch, 18th)

Fudian Bank Smelts

Gejiu Tin Ore

(Kunming) The tin in Gejiu has traditionally been smelted by local methods, with the resulting tin having a purity of only 92-93%. The tin smelting company established by the new Fudian Bank uses new methods, and its purity has reached about 99%. Although Yunnan has established an Import and Export Trade Commission to control export trade, the export of tin is still handled by the new Fudian Bank. (Dispatch, 18th)

Seventy Percent of Japanese People Suffer from Venereal Diseases 6

100,000 Die of Lung Disease Each Year, Infant Mortality Rate Continues to Rise

(Tokyo) Yamada, a member of the Japanese Diet, recently urged the Diet to pay attention to the serious state of health of the Japanese people. Yamada's statements were quite discouraging, as he stated that no less than 70% of the Japanese population suffers from venereal diseases. One million new cases of lung disease occur each year, resulting in 100,000 deaths annually. The high infant mortality rate is also increasing the death toll. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Chinese Industrial Cooperative Movement: A Grand Plan Underway 7

Hopes to Establish Cooperative Associations in Guerrilla Areas to Supply Chinese Army Needs and Prevent Japanese Goods Sales

(Chongqing) Alec, Deputy Director of the Chinese Industrial Cooperative Movement, has returned here today after departing from Jiangxi and inspecting cooperative centers in the Northwest provinces. It is said that the Chinese Industrial Cooperative Movement is currently undertaking a large-scale plan. The objectives of this movement are: (1) to supply the industrial needs of the interior during wartime; (2) to help solve the wartime refugee problem; (3) to help solve the problem of disabled soldiers; and (4) to reduce the need for imported goods. This movement hopes to establish cooperative associations in the guerrilla areas to meet the needs of the guerrillas and prevent the sale of Japanese goods in the occupied areas. This movement began last autumn after Alec traveled from Shanghai to Wuhan and presented his plan to Chinese leaders. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and President H.H. Kung have expressed their concern for this. According to a spokesperson for the movement, there are currently five headquarters, one each in the Northwest provinces, the Southwest provinces, the Southeast provinces, the Sichuan-Kang provinces, and Yunnan province. A total of 179 industrial cooperatives have been established. It is hoped that the number will reach about 500 within two months. The goal of this movement is to establish 30,000 industrial cooperatives throughout the country. It is now planned to establish industrial cooperatives in the interior to develop small-scale industries. According to Alec, although there are many Chinese laborers, they are not intellectuals, but they quickly understand the meaning of cooperation. He was particularly impressed by this point. He happily observed female factory workers in the Northwest provinces working in the giant caves of the mountains. They had been evacuated from Hankou to the Northwest through the efforts of Madame Chiang Kai-shek. In response to Mr. Alec's questions, they unanimously stated that they hoped to continue their current lives and did not want to return to factory life in Hankou. Currently, several locations have a daily business volume of as much as 10,000 yuan. Those in charge of this movement have recently appealed for continued capital allocation to expand this movement to all parts of China. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Yanping Fire

Yanping: At 0:15 this morning, a fire broke out suddenly at the Hejin Inn on Zhongshan Road, Yanping, burning more than 30 houses. The loss amounted to more than 100,000 yuan. The essence of the Yanping urban area has been reduced to ashes. The fire was extinguished at 4:30. (Dispatch, 18th)

French Chamber of Deputies Passes Government's Full Powers Bill 8

France is Embarking on the Path of War Preparation; Premier Stresses the Seriousness of the Situation

(Paris) Since the Chamber of Deputies granted French Premier Daladier the dictatorial power to deal with omnipotent countries, France has embarked on the basis of war. This power is only seen since the Clemenceau cabinet in the Great War. The power requested by the French Premier in the original proposal is limited to November of this year, and may be extended if necessary. When the Chamber of Deputies voted yesterday, the Socialist Party proposed two counter-proposals, which were both rejected by 316 votes to 262 and 328 votes to 254. The bill has now been submitted to the Senate, which is expected to pass it in the same way. The cabinet is scheduled to meet today and tomorrow to discuss how to promote measures to enhance France's military and industrial strength. (Associated Press dispatch, 19th)

(Paris) The full powers bill proposed by the government, after being discussed twice in the Chamber of Deputies, was passed by a vote of 321 to 264. Beforehand, many amendments proposed by members of the opposition parties were rejected one by one. Premier Daladier also delivered a tough speech, stressing that this bill must not be altered by a single word. He said that if the country encounters an emergency in the future, the government must take various measures to deal with it within hours, and it is impossible not to have full powers. The situation of the Chamber of Deputies meeting is recorded as follows:

(1) At the meeting of the Chamber of Deputies this morning, Schmidt, the reporter of the Finance Committee, immediately submitted a review report, saying that various military measures occupy a larger position, and it is important to expedite the manufacture of military equipment and stockpile raw materials. Right-wing member Grilis continued to speak, stating that the current situation was caused by the Munich Agreement. If a war occurs in the future, its danger will be greater than six months ago. How can we give full powers to the signatories of the Munich Agreement? Bergerie, a left-wing independent member, advocated national unity and convening a world economic conference to discuss the promotion of international trade. Maran, leader of the right-wing Republican Federation, expressed his trust in Premier Daladier. Essgarde-Figeac, a centralist member, said that after the Czech incident, reconciliation between France and Italy was easier than before. The Chamber of Deputies immediately rejected the amendments proposed by the opposition parties by a vote of 334 to 258.

(2) At the afternoon meeting, Communist leader Dougroux and Socialist member Mounet successively spoke, both opposing the government's full powers bill. Right-wing members Roland and Hélo stated that they were willing to vote in favor. Premier Daladier then delivered a speech, stating that the French government has lodged a strong protest against Germany's annexation of Czechoslovakia. The situation is so serious that empty words cannot solve the problem. The reason for requesting the passage of the full powers bill is to quickly respond to major incidents. This is a "matter of hours" and cannot be delayed. Members, please answer with yes or no. If you want to amend it, even a single word is unacceptable to me. Although there are many thorns ahead, I firmly believe that my compatriots will be able to work together to overcome them. Even if some people do not think it is possible, I will ignore them and continue to move forward. At this point, we must intensify our efforts. The government may require workers across the country to increase working hours and take other more resolute measures. It is also possible that the term of office of members of the Chamber of Deputies may be extended. After the Premier finished speaking, the Chamber of Deputies immediately put the government's original proposal to a vote and finally passed it by a vote of 321 to 264. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(Paris) After the full powers bill was passed by the Chamber of Deputies yesterday, the Senate Finance Committee immediately submitted it for review in the afternoon of today and decided to submit it to the Senate for discussion in the afternoon. It is expected to pass and be established by a large majority. As for the measures that the government intends to take, there are two types: (1) Regarding the number of army personnel, after a large number of Spanish government soldiers fled to France, the French authorities continued to increase the number of troops stationed on the southern border to be responsible for surveillance. The defense of other places is therefore not without impact, so it is necessary to replenish the number of army personnel to compensate. (2) Regarding military equipment, the number of manufactured items is increased and various important raw materials are purchased in preparation for emergencies. In addition, the current wartime national organization law may also be amended so that various factories and their workers can be requisitioned when necessary. (Havas, 19th)

German Influence Continues Eastward, Soviet Union is Highly Concerned 9

Romania Already Feels Threatened, Appeals to Allied Nations for Real Assistance

(Moscow) Last night, all sectors of the Soviet Union remained silent regarding possible actions the Soviet Union might take to respond to German pressure on Romania, awaiting official release of information on the matter. This silence does not indicate that the Soviet authorities do not take seriously any action that might bring their most dangerous enemy, Germany, closer to their borders. Well-informed sources believe that if Romania's integrity is threatened, the Soviet Union will have no choice but to deal with it with strong measures, especially because the Soviet Union's interests in Ukraine will be significantly affected. These strong measures may be similar to those used in the Sino-Japanese War. After Japan's invasion of China, the Soviet Union established friendly relations with China and provided material assistance. Stalin's remarks at the Communist Party Congress on March 10, stating that Germany's future expansionary actions would be westward, seem to indicate that Germany's recent actions have startled the Soviet Union. However, it must not be forgotten that the swallowing of Czechoslovakia after the Munich Agreement was already expected. In addition, another passage in Stalin's speech, stating, "We intend to provide assistance to countries that have suffered aggression and are fighting for national independence, and it is also worth looking back," is noteworthy. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

(London) Tonight, newspapers published news of Romania's deployment of troops. Although Romania's mobilization has not been officially acknowledged, the *Evening Standard* said that Bucharest had issued a mobilization order for five army corps. King Carol of Romania has stated to the British government that if Britain and France can provide assistance, Poland, Bulgaria, Romania, Greece, Turkey, and Yugoslavia can unanimously insist. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Bucharest, Romania. Although the official authorities here have solemnly denied the news about Germany's ultimatum to Romania, public opinion is still concerned about it. They believe that Germany's intention to gradually expand its influence in Romania can no longer be concealed. The approach of German troops to the Romanian border is enough to cause anxiety. Those in charge say that Romania must obtain the full assistance of its allies and friendly countries in order to negotiate with Germany on an equal footing. At the same time, public opinion in Yugoslavia, Poland, and even Bulgaria has changed, and all disapprove of Germany's actions. This is very comforting. The key to future events lies in seizing the opportunity and uniting with each other. What is unknowable is whether the Hungarian government will sacrifice its independence to serve Germany. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Prague, Czech Republic. Most of the German troops here have withdrawn and are reportedly moving eastward. Today, the Czech capital is quiet, and there have been no military impediments to transportation. However, planes soar through the sky all day long. German police have now replaced German soldiers on the streets. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Eastern Europe Forms Defensive Line to Prevent German Expansion 10

British Foreign Secretary Strongly Advocates in Cabinet Meeting; Changing Times Force Britain to Shift Policy

(London) According to reliable sources, the cabinet meeting held this afternoon focused on the German threat to Romania. It approved Prime Minister Chamberlain's speech in Birmingham. Foreign Secretary Halifax also reported in detail on the Central European situation, taking into account the information sent from the capitals of Czechoslovakia, Germany, and Romania. He also explained the situation regarding the British government's protest to Germany and the recall of the British Ambassador to Germany, Henderson. The cabinet immediately approved it. Foreign Secretary Halifax then expressed his opinion, advocating that a defensive line be formed from Poland, through Romania and Greece, to Turkey, to prevent Germany's continued eastward expansion. Although this proposal was opposed by Chancellor of the Exchequer Simon and several other cabinet members, Prime Minister Chamberlain and most of the cabinet members expressed their support. Once French President Lebrun comes to visit next week and the two sides conduct official talks, a firm decision can be made. In addition, Foreign Secretary Halifax also reported on his meetings with French Ambassador Corbin, Soviet Ambassador Maisky, German Ambassador Dirksen, and American Ambassador Kennedy. According to reports, Ambassador Maisky expressed his disappointment after the Munich Agreement, but if countries take collective action at this time to prevent Germany from expanding its influence, it should still be supported. When he later met with Ambassador Dirksen, he protested to him and informed him that the British government was determined to take the most resolute attitude. He then informed Ambassador Kennedy that the British government was gradually implementing a concrete policy of resisting aggression. According to general knowledge, the cabinet will discuss the military deployment commonly adopted in peacetime within the next week, and the issue of conscription should be included. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(London) Today's newspapers paid great attention to Romania's request for British assistance after receiving Germany's economic ultimatum and the consequences of this move, and published terrifying descriptions of the European crisis. It also reported that a new line of great powers, led by Britain, France, and the Soviet Union, and supported by Poland, Romania, Greece, Turkey, and Yugoslavia, has been proposed and is being discussed openly. According to several diplomatic correspondents, this proposal was discussed at the cabinet meeting last night, but no decision was made pending completion of consultations with the various dominions. In addition, there are many reports that the four great peace nations of Britain, the United States, France, and the Soviet Union may convene a meeting to discuss a common policy. The newspapers do not try to reveal Germany's current intentions, as they believe that this secret is tightly wrapped up between Hitler and his close advisors who met in Vienna last night. The newspapers everywhere remind the public that German troops are moving eastward and their destination is still unknown. According to the Warsaw correspondent of the *Sunday Times*, Poland and Hungary, which share a common border that Germany must pass through to advance into Romania, have begun political and military discussions. There are also reports that talks between the two countries will begin today. According to the diplomatic correspondent of the *Sunday Times*, Romanian Ambassador Tilea told British Foreign Secretary Halifax on Friday that 44 German divisions were partly in Czechoslovakia and the rest were mobilizing in Germany and were prepared to move eastward. Romanian opinion believes that even if Germany is preparing to attack Romania, this military action cannot be realized within ten days. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

(London) According to observations from diplomatic circles in various countries here, Chamberlain's speech in Birmingham yesterday marked Britain's abandonment of its appeasement policy. It was a statement of Britain's past policies toward Germany, and a statement that British-German relations had returned to the same state they were on the eve of the outbreak of the Great War. In short, the British Prime Minister's speech was the biggest change in Britain's domestic and foreign policies since the Great War. In his speech, Mr. Chamberlain had already acknowledged that his appeasement policy had completely failed. Mr. Zhang's question about Germany's annexation of Czechoslovakia being the first step in conquering the world by force was exactly the same as the various fears that Britain had about Germany on the eve of the Great War. The result of Germany's actions is to promote closer cooperation between Britain and France, which can be seen more clearly from French President Lebrun's visit to London on Tuesday. (Associated Press dispatch, 18th)

Germany Submits

Economic Proposal to Romania

Reports in British Newspapers Confirmed to be Facts; Germany Denies Issuing Ultimatum

(London) Regarding the news that Germany has submitted an economic proposal to Romania, the diplomatic affairs correspondent of Havas has learned that the news carried by the *Times* day before yesterday is completely accurate, but it is slightly inaccurate to say that it was an ultimatum. The denial issued by Germany is intended to save face. According to reports, the *Times* has reported that Walter, a German economist, has made two demands to the Romanian government: (1) Romania should gradually abandon its industrial construction plan, successively close existing factories, and focus on developing agriculture; (2) Various products such as grains, oil, wood, and livestock can only be sold to Germany. If the above can be followed, Germany is prepared to guarantee Romania's territorial integrity and national independence. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(Berlin) Rumors that Germany has submitted an ultimatum to Romania have recently been denied by semi-official circles here, calling it unfounded and saying that the economic negotiations currently underway between Germany and Romania are only aimed at developing bilateral trade. The various rumors are intended to increase the tension of the international situation and should not be believed. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Soviet Union's Criticism of German Government; Does Not Recognize German Annexation of Czechoslovakia 11

Also Denies Making Promises to Aid Romania; British and French Protests Rejected by Germany

(Moscow) The Soviet government has sent a note to the German government stating its non-recognition of Germany's occupation of Czechoslovakia, saying: "The Soviet government cannot but regard the German military occupation of various provinces of Czechoslovakia and subsequent actions of the German government as autocratic, tyrannical, and aggressive. In the Soviet government's view, the German government's actions not only run counter to the elimination of dangers to universal peace, but also create and increase such dangers. The German government has undermined the political stability of Eastern Europe, increased the factors of alarm, and dealt a new blow to the sense of tranquility of the people of Central Europe." Regarding the rumor that Romania had received a concrete promise of Soviet assistance, qualified sources in the Soviet Union say that Romania had not requested aid from the Soviet Union, nor had the Soviet Union given any promises. German Aggression Against Other Nations; Economy Followed by Politics 12

Intends to Use Methods Against Hungary on Romania

Sufficient to Promote Unity of Democratic Front

(London) A Reuters diplomatic correspondent reports that Foreign Secretary Halifax today discussed the situation arising from Romania's appeal for British aid to resist German economic demands with the ambassadors of France, the Soviet Union, the United States. It is heard that liaison between Britain and Romania has now been intensified, and Romania's determination to resist German aggression with all its strength has also been strengthened. The news obtained by London yesterday regarding German economic demands on Romania was originally what the Romanian side wished to publish, but the Romanian capital later denied it, presumably in the hope that Germany might change its position. Recalling that after the settlement of the Sudetenland issue last September, Germany made similar demands on Hungary, restricting it to being an agricultural country and limiting its military strength. Now that Germany has drawn Hungary into its economic sphere and placed the Hungarian army in an insignificant position, it is preparing to continue its steps to annex territories closer to Vienna, starting with the economy and then continuing with politics. It is believed that the British Cabinet will discuss Britain's attitude towards this and the results of the Foreign Secretary's contact with various diplomats this morning at its meeting this afternoon. Although the German side stated that the German Ambassador's meeting with the British Foreign Secretary was a routine matter, it is certain that the British Foreign Secretary took this opportunity to reiterate to the German Ambassador Britain's position that the occupation of Czechoslovakia cannot be regarded as legal. Moreover, the harmonious relationship between the British and French nations is close and seamless, and this will be fully demonstrated. Regarding this matter, France's position is very clear. Germany Levies Punitive Taxes on Imports; United States Applies Economic Pressure on Germany 13

Applicable to Japan and Other Treaty-Breaking Countries

Does Not Recognize German Annexation of Czechoslovakia as Legal; Will Take Parallel Actions with Britain, France, and Soviet Union

(Washington) The U.S. government announced last night that, in retaliation for Germany's aggression in Europe and its attempts to use economic power to invade the Western Hemisphere, the U.S. government will impose a "punitive tax" on German imports. This tax will take effect on March 23rd. Congress expects that the government will also use such restrictive measures against Japan and other countries that violate treaties. The Treasury Department also announced that the government had notified Britain and France of the imposition of a "punitive tax" on German imports. The U.S. State Department yesterday condemned the Nazi Party in very sharp language and decided to retaliate against Germany's actions in Czechoslovakia. According to information revealed by Under Secretary of State Welles, the United States will send a note to Germany stating the American people's resentment of the Nazi Party's annexation of Czechoslovakia. It is expected that the note will express in clear and direct terms that the United States will definitely refuse to recognize Germany's seizure of Czechoslovakia as legal. Welles said that the note will respond to Berlin's official note regarding the Nazi Party's occupation of Bohemia and Moravia. The United States, Britain, and France are taking the same stance and will unanimously refuse to recognize Germany's occupation of Czechoslovakia. However, regarding external reports that Britain intends to convene a four-power conference, including the three democratic countries and the Soviet Union, to plan to stop German aggression, Welles said he had heard nothing about it. (Associated Press, 19th)

(Washington) According to news from here today, the "punitive tax" announced by the Treasury Department on German imports will, in addition to collecting ordinary higher tax rates, also levy 25% as a "punishment." Commercial experts say that this new tax may reduce the import of Nazi Party goods into the United States to a very low level. It is heard that the Treasury Department's announcement was based on the opinion of U.S. Comptroller General McCarl, who believes that Germany's subsidies for U.S. exports in order to exchange for U.S. cotton, reaching 33.33%, are very inappropriate. Recently, Germany has been implementing subsidies for general exporters due to its weak business. (Associated Press, 19th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt, in his message to Congress on January 4th, said that apart from resorting to war, he intended to apply pressure to aggressor countries. Government officials recently declared that the U.S. government now intends to implement this pressure on Germany. The measures already decided include the following: (1) The various preferential treatments previously given by the United States to Czechoslovakia in commerce and finance will now be cancelled, and Germany will not be allowed to inherit these preferential treatments. (2) An additional 25% tax will be levied on German imports. In addition to these two measures, the U.S. will not recognize the new situation in Central Europe and believes that the Czech people's surrender is only a temporary situation. This expression by the United States contains the unofficial meaning of encouraging Czechoslovakia. After Under Secretary of State Welles made a formal declaration condemning Germany, Britain and France immediately issued similar statements and formally protested. Such parallel actions by the three countries will certainly strengthen President Roosevelt's position, which is indeed a very gratifying phenomenon. More generally, the international situation has undergone profound changes. The appeasement policy towards the European situation has also ceased to be implemented after Prime Minister Chamberlain delivered a speech in Birmingham. Peace-loving countries must have realized that the only way to stop Germany from continuing to annex territories in Europe is to rely on force. Especially since Germany's actions are not yet its main stage, because its desires do not stop there, the current situation is unlikely to be stabilized from this point on. The U.S. government, regardless of the opposition of isolationists, resolutely demanded the amendment of the current Neutrality Act to strengthen the resistance of democratic countries. This is why. (Havas, 18th)

Pittman to Propose Amendment to Neutrality Act 15

Belligerents Purchase Arms from the United States; Transaction to be Based on Cash

(Washington) Senate Foreign Relations Committee Chairman Pittman is scheduled to submit a new legislative bill to the Senate on the 20th of this month, advocating the repeal of the current Neutrality Act and authorizing the President to (1) designate belligerents within 30 days of the outbreak of war, (2) once belligerents are designated, U.S. merchant ships shall not load goods to be transported to those countries, (3) all belligerents may purchase various items from the United States, including weapons, but must purchase them with cash and transport them themselves, (4) prohibiting loans or credits to belligerents, (5) the above provisions shall not apply to any American countries that do not participate in wars outside of the Americas. (Havas, 18th)

(Washington) Since Senate Foreign Relations Committee Chairman Pittman announced that he would propose an amendment to the U.S. current Neutrality Act in Congress, it is generally expected here that the United States will increase its economic pressure and unfriendly economic actions on dictatorial countries. Pittman's amendment will give the U.S. President broader discretionary power to sell arms to "countries that should go to war and countries that should not go to war," and transactions will be based on cash. According to Pittman, if this case can be established, there is no need for the President to declare the existence of a state of war for the Sino-Japanese War; this law can automatically apply. The case stipulates that "regardless of whether or not declaration procedures have been followed, the President may declare a list of countries involved in the war after 30 days of war and apply the cash transaction method." According to Pittman, the UK will definitely benefit more from this method. (AP, 19th)

New Neutrality Act Contains Four Key Points

(Washington) In addition to what is seen in another telegram, the main points of the Neutrality Act amendment proposed by Pittman are as follows: This case also advocates authorizing the President to prohibit U.S. citizens and all ships from going to specially designated war zones after the outbreak of war, but with several provisos to facilitate Red Cross relief work. Pittman recently gave a speech saying that there are four key points to the bill he drafted: (1) It does not apply to foreign civil wars. If Congress can vote on this case before the end of the Spanish Civil War, the measure prohibiting the transport of arms to Spain will naturally be withdrawn. (2) Countries that do not have large-scale arms factories can purchase weapons from the United States during wartime. The unfairness of the current Neutrality Act is thus corrected. (3) The advantages actually occupied by major naval powers are thus determined. (4) U.S. private arms factories can develop more easily, which is inherently beneficial to national defense. (5) The foreign sales channels of U.S. weapons can be preserved. A certain congressman proposed a motion to simply abolish the current Neutrality Act. He believes that although this law is incomplete, the issue of national neutrality should be governed by appropriate provisions, and he therefore proposed this amendment based on his limited knowledge. It is not authorized by the government. Political figures recently commented that Pittman's case is indeed part of the government's plan. Its main purpose is to give President Roosevelt greater freedom of action so that he can easily assist the democratic countries in the event of war in Europe. (Havas, 18th)

The Campaign Slogs On Without Success, and Friction Intensifies: Conflict Between Japanese Naval and Army Forces in Guangdong 16

Yokohama Specie Bank Suffers Huge Losses

Shantou Dispatch: According to military sources in Huiyang, the Potian Brigade from Taiwan recently appeared between Dongguan, Taiping, and Chashan. The Japanese troops from Shilong, after withdrawing on the 8th, suddenly turned back and reinforced with two additional regiments, establishing strongholds in Futian, Zhengguo, Changping, and Shitan, with the intention of attacking Luofu Mountain again. The Japanese army has been invading Guangzhou for five months, but the campaign slogs on without success. The naval and army forces have different strategies and compete for leadership, leading to intensified friction. The "Good Citizen Certificates" issued by the Japanese army are not recognized in the tributaries of the Pearl River. From Humen Taiping to Huangpu, Nantoutou, and the south of Henan, the area is under naval control. People carrying cloth-based Good Citizen Certificates are often seen having them torn up by the Japanese navy. The Japanese army is now using wooden Good Citizen Certificates to prevent the navy from tearing them up. Naval plainclothes personnel entering and leaving the urban areas are also often bullied. Taiwanese and Korean soldiers can only lower their heads and suffer in silence, not daring to argue. At noon on the 6th, more than ten marines from the Tajima landing force disembarked at Nantoutou and marched into Guangzhou city, clashing with army sentries. Gunfire erupted immediately, causing great chaos in the city. Criminals took the opportunity to loot. It is reported that Yokohama Specie Bank lost more than 200,000 yuan in banknotes, and there were many casualties. (March 10th)

Ms. Sterling Speaks

The People of Guangxi Province Are Filled with Patriotic Fervor

The Government Does Its Best to Care for Refugees

Continental Daily News reports that Ms. Sterling, of the Southern Baptist Church, who has just arrived in Shanghai from Guilin, told reporters yesterday (the 18th) that the Guangxi Provincial Government has achieved remarkable results in handling the heavy burden caused by the war and does not attempt to shift its responsibility to others. Although refugees are pouring into Guilin from all directions, the provincial government is taking care of them in a systematic way. Although I have not witnessed it myself, I have heard that registration offices have been set up every ten li along major transportation routes. Refugees fill in their names at the registration offices, and the authorities provide free transportation to the extremely poor and give them three dimes in silver each day. In the past two months, frequent morning rains have prevented Guilin from being bombed by Japanese planes. During this period, although several air raid alerts were heard, no bombs were dropped. Whenever the air raid sirens sounded, a rare spectacle occurred: the 200,000 residents of Guilin climbed the specially built steps, crossed the city walls, and went to the stone caves in the nearby mountains for temporary shelter. During the air raid alerts, although all civilians evacuated, the police remained at their posts. If a house was hit by a bomb, the local police would guard the property until the homeowner returned home. If someone's residence was destroyed, the authorities would provide some public buildings for them to live in until they could build a new house. After the outbreak of the war, the daily routine has changed. Due to the risk of air raids in the morning, business must be conducted between 3:00 PM and midnight. Although there have been no air raids in the past two months, there have been bombings before, and half of the houses in the city have been destroyed. As for industrial cooperatives, none have been established in Guilin yet, but preliminary investigations are underway. Commerce in Guilin seems quite prosperous. People everywhere are preparing to resist the Japanese army, and signs of military activity can be seen everywhere. The Friends of Wounded Soldiers Association, a group that helps wounded soldiers, is carrying out arduous tasks in Guilin.

Chinese Troops in Northern Jiangsu

Closing in on Huaiyin

Fierce Fighting at Zhaoguan Dam

Taixian Correspondence: The Japanese army has decided to launch a large-scale invasion of northern Jiangsu and has successively invaded the counties of Huai, Si, Fu, and Bao. Except for the fact that the Chinese troops recovered Suijing quickly, so losses were relatively minor, the losses in other places such as Siyang, Lianshui, Donghai, Muyang, Funing, Huaiyin, and Huaian were very heavy. According to an investigation, although most of the residents of Huaiyin had been evacuated before it was abandoned and public utilities had been destroyed, the Japanese army looted miscellaneous items from the people after capturing the city and transported away more than 200 boxes. More than 200 civilians were shot dead, and countless rapes occurred. Furthermore, Funing was heavily bombed by Japanese planes, and after they briefly invaded the county seat, most of the houses in the city were reduced to ashes, and countless residents were massacred. The county was recovered by Chinese troops the day before yesterday, and efforts are being made to appease the local people. The other counties also suffered severely from looting, and the situation is still under investigation. Huaiyin and Haizhou are now under siege and counterattack by a new force of Chinese troops and armed civilians, and the fighting is extremely intense. There is a rumor that the county seat of Huaiyin has already been recovered by Chinese troops. Also, more than 200 Japanese soldiers from Shaobo lightly attacked the Chinese army's Zhaoguan Dam position at noon on the 10th, with heavy artillery fire. The Chinese defenders bravely resisted, and after fierce fighting until the afternoon, the Japanese army was defeated and retreated. Dozens of Japanese soldiers were killed and many were wounded in this battle, and a large number of bullets were consumed. The Chinese side suffered no significant losses, and the Chen position remained as solid as a rock. On the morning of the 12th, the Japanese army used six trucks to transport wounded Japanese soldiers and corpses from Shaobo to Yangzhou. On the morning of the 12th, Japanese troops at Huangjue Bridge in Xishan, Yangzhou, had contact with Chinese guerrillas. On the morning of the 13th, there was also artillery fire in the southwest of Yangzhou. It is reported that the Doujia Bridge was raided by Chinese troops, and the Japanese army also suffered casualties.

Desolate Scene in Suqian

No Commerce Within the City

The North-China Daily News reports that Suqian fell on November 22nd last year. On December 2nd and 3rd, the Chinese army counterattacked the city, causing heavy losses to the Japanese army in terms of manpower and equipment, but failed to recover it. Since then, no counterattack has been launched, but the Chinese army is still within five miles northeast of the city (as of February 27th). Most of the Chinese troops are on the east bank of the Grand Canal, while Suqian is on the west bank. The Chinese troops in the vicinity include various units such as the Central Army, the Jiangsu Provincial Army, and guerrillas. Their artillery and mechanized equipment are not sufficient for an offensive, but they have shown astonishing strength in defense. The 57th Division is generally considered to be the best trained and equipped among the troops in northern Jiangsu.

Although Suqian has been lost

for three months, the city is still on the front line. Anyone with experience knows what this means. The city gates of Suqian's outer city are heavily guarded, and no one is allowed to enter or leave. Moreover, in some respects, the regulations are now stricter than before. Those with "Good Citizen Certificates" were once allowed to enter and leave, but even they have not been allowed to enter or leave freely for several weeks. Every five days, those with "Good Citizen Certificates" can enter the city, but under no circumstances can they leave again. Unless some changes occur, they are virtually prisoners. At the beginning of Suqian's fall, American expatriates could enter and leave the city gates, but now they cannot. Since the establishment of the local puppet regime, the five American missionaries in Suqian have lived in houses outside the south side of the city, establishing a refugee camp. The entrance of the house is only sixty yards from the south city gate. A machine gun nest is built close to the house, so the house is surrounded on three sides. Every night, the Japanese army shoots aimlessly and incessantly, to intimidate the Chinese troops who are patrolling or operating in the suburbs. The artillery inside the city also often

Opens Fire in Response

and randomly throws grenades everywhere. Anyone who complains about the sounds of Shanghai at night can try sleeping in this house for one night. The refugee camp once housed seven or eight hundred people, including hospital employees. Currently, there are fewer than six hundred people. Most of the refugees buy their own food to cook, and those who are penniless receive free food twice a day. So far, the supply of food and fuel has not been completely interrupted, but fuel was once scarce and expensive. It is probably unnecessary to elaborate on the general business situation, which is extremely bad. Since the fall of Suqian, no one in the city is engaged in any kind of commerce. Recently, a Korean person opened a store selling sugar, beer, cigarettes, and canned goods. Some Chinese merchants have transported most of their goods from the city to villages and towns to avoid air raids. Now some of these goods are sold in the villages, towns, and local markets. Trade in local products is quite prosperous in some small town markets. Imported goods are becoming increasingly scarce. Homes are destroyed, families are scattered, and there are many grieving people. It is undoubtedly a tragic period in recent history.

Li Bai's Wartime History

He Achieved Merit Early in His Military Career

Interview with Zhang Guoquan

Among the military and political personnel of Guangxi, no one does not know "Teacher Zhang." He is from Yangshuo and was a teacher of Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, Huang Xuchu, Huang Shaohong, and others in their youth. Even now, they still call him "Teacher Zhang." Therefore, everyone also calls him "Teacher Zhang" instead of his name. Perhaps he is the only surviving teacher of these four gentlemen, and I did not want to miss the opportunity to interview him. Teacher Zhang's residence is on Xianqian Street, less than fifty steps from the county government. It faces east and is a stone-lintelled house with two bays, which looks newly built. A robust child handed in my business card. I initially thought he was Teacher Zhang's grandson, but later learned that he was his only beloved son. After a moment, a servant brought out tea and cigarettes. Then "Teacher Zhang," wearing a dark gray silk wide robe and a pair of cloth shoes, came out from the inner building to meet me. Although he was already fifty-six years old, he had not yet grown a beard and looked at least ten years younger than his age. His steady gait and firm handshake showed that he had a youthful period in military life. I first expressed my greetings and explained the purpose of my visit. Teacher Zhang graduated from the first class of the Baoding Xiehe Class, the predecessor of the Baoding Military Academy, at the end of the Qing Dynasty. The Governor-General was Duan Qirui, and the Superintendent was Qu Tongfeng. There were infantry, cavalry, artillery, engineering, and transport departments, and the course lasted two and a half years. After the second class of the Xiehe Class graduated, it was renamed the Baoding Military Academy. During the reign of Emperor Xuantong, he graduated from the Japanese Military Academy and returned to China with Cai Songpo from Yunnan, Zhuang Yunkuan from Jiangsu, and others. He founded the Army Elementary School in Guilin, Guangxi. Li Bai and the two Huangs were the first students of this elementary school. At that time, these "distinguished students" were only teenagers, but among the more than one hundred students, he felt that they were "endowed with great talent" and "diligent in learning." "I am not saying this now because they are all in prominent positions. I am not trying to flatter them or boast," Teacher Zhang said. "De Lin and Jian Sheng are indeed astute and courageous. In the early years of the Republic of China, I led troops, and De Lin served as a company commander under me. Once during a battle in Hunan, his cheek was pierced by a bullet. I told him to withdraw, but he persisted until the task was completed before leaving the battlefield. After he recovered, a battalion commander position happened to be vacant, so I promoted him. Jian Sheng, while suppressing bandits in southern Guangxi Province, unfortunately broke his leg. Although he was sent to Guangdong for treatment and recovered, he still limps somewhat when walking. His decisiveness was evident from a young age." He said that he was originally a member of the proletariat, and the new house he now lives in was built for him last year by these "classmates." He used to live in Hong Kong and often goes to Guilin after returning to his hometown. "I either stay at Li's house or eat at Bai's house." He is truly a respectable teacher. On the evening of the very day I interviewed him, Teacher Zhang actually walked along the muddy village road to the Lequn Society to return my visit, which I found to be an honor I did not deserve. That evening, he was wearing a leather hat and holding a copper-tipped bamboo dry tobacco pipe, showing some signs of age, but he was in high spirits. He spoke a lot about the customs and local conditions of Yangshuo. It was already dark when he left. He smiled and said, "After you come to Yangshuo for fun, you should pay us some taxes." I also smiled and said, "Alright then!" He said, "Please write more articles in the newspapers to attract more tourists to our local area." I wanted to send him back, but he insisted on refusing, saying, "In my own home, everyone should lead the way." I had no choice but to give up. Zhang also inscribed the words "National Golden Voice" for this newspaper. Teacher Zhang's name is Guoquan, and his courtesy name is Zhenou. He is currently a lieutenant general参军 in the Fifth Route Army Headquarters. He often makes suggestions on military planning to Li Bai, which are often adopted. (The End)

In the last three minutes, Clark and Oakley each scored, and Donghua was defeated 4-1. Eradicating Illiteracy in Guangxi This Year 24

Designating This Year as Adult Education Year, Raising One Million in Funds, Mobilizing Six Thousand Teachers

Guangxi Province has been working hard to eliminate illiteracy for the past four years, reducing it by more than 1.5 million. There are still more than 1.82 million adults who are out of school. This year is specifically designated as the Adult Education Year, with the aim of eradicating illiteracy within one year, strengthening public mobilization work, and leveraging the power of resistance against Japan and national reconstruction. The implementation plan has been approved, and it has been decided to establish provincial and county-level adult education year promotion committees. In mid-March, inspectors were dispatched to all districts in the province to cooperate with the administrative commissioners of each district, convening third-section chiefs from subordinate counties to discuss and then go to each county to form promotion committees and begin work. Nearly one million in funding has been raised, and it has been decided to mobilize six thousand teachers to teach illiterate adults of both sexes aged 18 to 45. Textbooks are provided by the government, stationery is provided by the students, and the study period is set at two months, two hours per day, without holidays.

Zhejiang Education Department Orders Provincial Schools to Increase Publicly Funded and Tuition-Free Spots, Universally Awarding and Assisting Poor Students to Enroll 25

(Jinhua Correspondence) The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, after investigating the fact that people's lives have been difficult since the War of Resistance, and they cannot afford to pay for their children's education, and the situation of young people dropping out of school is becoming increasingly serious, in order to relieve those who have dropped out of school, it was decided last year that all provincial schools would be exempt from tuition fees starting from the first semester of the 27th year. Now, within the budget of the provincial education and culture expenses for the 28th year, the number of publicly funded spots will be increased so that poor students can benefit more. The department has now made overall arrangements, and starting from this semester, the number of publicly funded and tuition-free spots for new students in specialized, high school, and junior high school programs will be increased to account for 14% of the class size, that is, 7 publicly funded and 7 tuition-free students per class of 50 people. For continuing students, a maximum of 2 additional students may be added to each category per class. The number of publicly funded spots for normal school and vocational students will be increased to account for 18% of the class size for new students, that is, 9 publicly funded students per class of 50 people, and a maximum of 4 additional students may be added to each category per class for continuing students. Except for the affiliated elementary school part, special orders are issued to each school to understand the government's purpose of awarding and assisting poor and outstanding students, and to properly handle it to benefit the impoverished.

Ningxia Province: Teacher Training: Establishing Two Provincial Normal Schools 27

As of the statistics of the 26th year, teacher training in Ningxia Province includes the Provincial Ningxia Normal School and the Provincial Zhongwei Normal School. The Provincial Ningxia Normal School is a simplified normal school, and the school buildings were newly built in the autumn of the 25th year, covering an area of approximately 15 mu. There is an auditorium that can accommodate 100 people, four large classrooms and offices, a library, and 30 dormitories for faculty and students, along with more than ten other rooms, totaling more than 50 rooms. The dormitories can accommodate about 120 boarders. In addition, there are two basketball and volleyball courts each. There are 71 students in grades 1, 2, and 3, 23 faculty members, and the monthly operating expenses are 2,210 yuan. Students are not charged any fees, and the school provides books and lecture notes. The Provincial Zhongwei Normal School was originally a junior high school, but was converted into a simplified normal school in the autumn of the 26th year. New school buildings were built, covering an area of more than 20 mu, which can accommodate about 200 boarders. There are grades 1 and 2, with 57 students, 16 faculty members, and monthly operating expenses of 1,201 yuan. Student benefits are the same as at Ningxia Normal School.
