Economic Section

China's Economic Diplomacy During Wartime 36

— Zhang Xiaomei

Dr. Zhang Xiaomei is a renowned economist both in China and abroad. She has served as the Director of the Economic Research Office of the Bank of China and has also been in charge of the China National Economic Research Institute. It is said that Dr. Zhang has also been appointed as the Deputy Director of the National Southwest Economic Research Institute, which is currently being prepared for establishment. This article is a chapter from Dr. Zhang's newly compiled "China and Foreign Economic Yearbook," which is published by the China National Economic Research Institute and is scheduled for sale on March 25th. We are deeply grateful to Dr. Zhang for allowing our publication to publish it in advance, and we hope our readers will pay attention to it. Editor.

(I) The Key to Victory or Defeat in Modern Warfare

In the World War of 1914, Germany single-handedly resisted and fought for four years, ultimately suffering defeat. This was not due to unfavorable conditions on the front lines, but rather to the inadequacy of the home front. General Ludendorff, based on his experience in the Great War, advocated the theory of total war, believing that in modern warfare there is no distinction between the front and the rear. Victory or defeat is determined not by the quantity of armaments but by the strength of the nation's resources. This is no longer limited to the clash of the two armies, but a struggle between two great nations.

As the ancient saying goes, "Victory or defeat is a common occurrence for military strategists." This is especially true today. Temporary gains or losses are not enough to be a key to victory. The endurance of the war, leading to final victory, depends on the resilience of the entire nation and the strength of the entire national economy, especially the latter as a prerequisite for the material basis of a long-term war of resistance.

Furthermore, modern international relations are intricate and complex. Disputes between two countries are often sufficient to trigger conflicts of interest involving related third countries or even the entire world. China, often referred to as a semi-colonial country, has always been a battleground for great powers. Japan's war against China is undoubtedly aimed at excluding the influence of Europe and America in the Far East, blockading China's door, and allowing Japan to enjoy it exclusively. Therefore, since the September 18th Incident, the Sino-Japanese conflict has long been a major performance on the international political stage. Since the July 7th Incident developed into the August 13th Battle, although the great powers have not actively performed due to various reasons, their spiritual and material sympathy and assistance to China have played a considerable role. Especially today, after the world has become aware of Japan's ambition to swallow China alone, they can no longer sit idly by. For example, Britain and the United States have successively presented Japan with strong diplomatic notes and have resolutely moved from spiritual sympathy for China to material assistance. Our country is fighting for independent survival and has national resources hundreds of times greater than Japan as its backing. Whether or not we can obtain foreign resources is not enough to sway our determination and real strength to win the war. However, obtaining foreign resources during wartime can indeed make the strength of the war of resistance more substantial. Moreover, our country's industry is backward, and modern military-industrial industry has no foundation to speak of. Therefore, striving for overseas resources is an indispensable step in the great cause of the war of resistance. The European War ended with the participation of the United States. On the surface, it was because the Allied Powers had this new force to join, and they were able to defeat the exhausted German army. In essence, it was because Germany was poor in resources, and therefore could not use overseas resources to make up for it, which led to its rapid collapse.

Our government, aware of this, ordered the stabilization of finance at the beginning of the war, engaged in the relocation of industries, promoted the industrial cooperative movement, and built the Southwest. It also developed resources, rectified the domestic economy, maintained credit, recognized the principle of open doors, expressed welcome to foreign investment, and worked hard to cooperate economically with friendly countries. Now, after a year and a half of the war of resistance, the currency system is stable, the economy is stable, and the international community praises it unanimously.

(II) The International Development of Resisting Aggression

Resisting aggression lies in our resolute resistance to the war until the final victory. If friends of our allies can uphold the principles of justice and humanity and take economic sanctions against the aggressors, their efforts will be doubled. This has already been mentioned earlier. Therefore, at the beginning of March 1938, the Chinese delegation in Beijing published the economic conditions for resisting Japan's aggression against China as follows:

(1) Prohibit the supply of military or industrial raw materials to Japan. Because Japan's military and industrial raw materials are largely dependent on foreign countries, if various countries stop supplying them, even if it is limited to a small number of major items, it will inevitably be severely hit.

(2) Boycott Japanese goods and Japanese ships. Japan's international balance of payments depends on the export of industrial products and its shipping income to achieve balance. If various countries boycott Japanese goods and Japanese ships, it will not only put its industry to death, but also destroy its entire national economy.

(3) Refuse credit to Japan. Japan's war expenses are huge, and domestic resources are limited. Without foreign credit, it will not be able to take care of itself, let alone develop the gains of aggression. If various countries refuse credit, not only will it not be able to obtain profits like the Sino-Japanese and Russo-Japanese wars, but it can also strengthen the effectiveness of points one and two.

(4) Economic measures of a considerable minority of countries. Because Japan's supply of raw materials and credit and the market for its exports are not concentrated in a small number of countries, these few countries include the United States, the British Empire, France, and Annam, the Netherlands, and the East Indies, Belgium, etc. If they sever economic relations with Japan, Japan will be like a fish out of water and unable to be active.

(5) Aid China. To strengthen China's ability to resist the war and resist international aggression, peace-loving countries should expand assistance to China and provide extensive military and financial assistance.

On the other hand, in early February 1938, the Executive Committee of the League of Nations passed a resolution to assist China, reiterating the resolution of the previous conference, asking countries to do their best to assist China. At the same time, the International Peace Movement convened an international boycott conference in London, attended by representatives from twenty countries, unanimously passing a boycott resolution, severely punishing acts of aggression. Subsequently, an international peace movement conference was convened in Paris, unanimously opposing Japan's indiscriminate killing of innocent people, resolving to boycott Japanese goods, stop the supply of military materials, encourage loans to China, and resolving to establish the China Relief General Association in London as the central hub of the international China relief movement. Since October of the same year, the association has also published an international China relief newsletter once a month to communicate and promote the development of China relief work in various places. Currently, the international China relief work supported by these international peace groups is generally advancing along the following three major lines: (1) Urging governments to implement the League of Nations' resolutions on sanctions against Japan? (2) Expanding the boycott of Japanese goods movement, (3) Donating money, donating medicines and clothing, and providing relief to Chinese wounded soldiers and refugees.

(III) Achievements of Our Country's Economic Diplomacy

The aforementioned China relief work is all automatically carried out by fair-minded people around the world, and all are implemented in the form of civil organizations, which cannot be regarded as the gains of our country's economic diplomacy. The one that is initiated by our government and can be regarded as economic diplomacy work is to strive for financial assistance from various countries to China. Among the current countries, the most sympathetic and influential ones are the three major democratic countries: Britain, the United States, and France. They are described separately below.

China and the United States: China and the United States are located on both sides of the Pacific Ocean and have always been friendly. Since the signing of the Nine-Power Treaty at the Washington Conference, they have become even more harmonious. When the September 18th Incident occurred, former Secretary of State Stimson strongly upheld justice and ran around to appeal, eventually leading to the passage of the non-recognition resolution by the League of Nations. When the Sino-Japanese War broke out in 1937, the Chinese people looked up to the United States very deeply. Although there are isolationists and absolute pacifists in American public opinion, most of them condemned aggression and sympathized with the war of resistance. Especially those with a slightly longer-term vision, such as Mr. Stimson and Emory Luccock D.D., pastor of the Shanghai International Church, all reminded the United States of its moral responsibility in the Sino-Japanese war and advocated for some active actions. Renowned Far East commentator Nathaniel Pfeffer also changed his original position of isolationism after observing the results of China's one-year war of resistance and advocated that Americans should not cooperate with the aggressor: "Do not buy (Japanese goods), do not sell (military supplies), do not lend (credit)"; at the same time, cooperate with non-aggressor countries and provide them with various conveniences. The sympathy of American public opinion towards China can be seen from this.

What is noteworthy about Sino-American economic relations after the war is the silver issue and the credit issue.

In 1934, the United States began its silver purchase policy, raising the price of silver. Eventually, China was unable to maintain the silver standard and announced the cessation of the silver standard in November 1935, adopting a managed exchange rate system. In the spring of 1936, Chinese banker Chen Guangfu was commissioned to visit the United States and signed a silver agreement with US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, in which the United States purchased 50 million taels of Chinese silver at a price of US$0.45 per tael.

In July 1937, the first Sino-American agreement expired. At that time, Finance Minister Kong attended the coronation ceremony of the British King and then traveled to the United States, where he renewed the silver agreement, exchanging silver for gold to be used as our country's exchange reserve and export credit guarantee.

In July 1938, the agreement expired again. In late July, the Japanese spread rumors that Britain intended to put China's gold reserves under international co-management. The US Treasury Secretary officially declared that the US purchase of Chinese silver had been extended, with conditions largely unchanged.

According to the August issue of Citibank Monthly: In May 1938, the Chinese government requested the US government to continue purchasing silver to help stabilize Sino-American monetary relations. The two sides then established a rollover agreement to exchange Chinese silver for US dollar credit or gold. In the first half of 1938, 140 million taels of Chinese silver were shipped to New York, worth US$63 million. Since October 1937, a total of 190 million taels of silver have been shipped, worth US$84 million. Since 1934, the United States has purchased a total of 300 million taels of Chinese silver, and the proceeds have been used to bid for gold and as bank deposits. This is an example of monetary cooperation between the United States and China.

However, the destruction of war is unlimited. Therefore, it is not enough to talk about long-term resistance to the war without making great efforts to build and develop resources, let alone talk about post-war revival. It is necessary to use foreign credit.

In late September 1938, the Chinese mission arrived in the United States, still led by banking magnate Mr. Chen Guangfu. On the one hand, they discussed the supply of military supplies and credit with the American business community, and on the other hand, they consulted with the American government on loans.

On October 20th, the US Treasury Department declared that progress had been made in discussions with the Chinese mission.

On December 16th, a US$25 million loan between China and the United States was completed. At the same time, there was also good news about the establishment of a Sino-British loan. This credit is for a period of five years and is purely commercial in nature. Most of it will be used to purchase trucks and gasoline. (To be continued)

Highlights of Famous Works

British Gold Reserves 37

— The Economist. No. 4976 Translated by Chen Baorong

Since the turmoil in Europe, London's position in world finance has declined along with its political position. The era of the British pound dominating the world has almost become a thing of the past. Consequently, the British government's gold reserves have been constantly lost and declined as the pound struggles. The London Economist also admits this frankly. However, based on the magazine's reporter's report on the local gold storage in South Africa, it can be seen that the foundation of the British pound is not as bad as people generally think. The magazine's reporter's proposal to re-evaluate the gold reserves of the Bank of England has now been implemented. Moreover, its view that the future of the British pound depends on the political situation in Europe is now being reflected. We are very grateful to Mr. Chen for translating and providing this article to our publication, and we hope that all those who care about British gold will pay attention to it. Editor.

Sharp Decline in Gold Reserves: The recent British Exchange Equalization Fund, as announced on December 31st of last year, is as follows: (Calculated at 140 shillings per ounce) (Unit: Million Pounds)

1937 1938

March 31st September 30th March 31st September 30th

Bank of England 516.6 537.6 537.6 537.6

Exchange Equalization Fund 186.9 279.3 297.8 151.8

Total 703.5 816.9 835.4 689.4

According to this, the Bank of England's gold reserves have remained stable throughout. However, the Exchange Equalization Fund lost £146 million in gold between April and September. The "Economist" magazine, published on October 22, 1938, estimated that the British Exchange Equalization Fund had lost at least £65 million by the end of May due to the withdrawal of French gold deposits in Britain. In the subsequent two months of August and September, another £100 million of gold had to be successively flowed out. Therefore, it was predicted that the Exchange Equalization Fund would have at most £130 million remaining by September 30th. Today's official report shows that the initial prediction was too pessimistic. Although: The difference between the prediction and the actual number is only £22 million, which seems to be excusable.

Establish a Foreign Treasury?: The average weekly amount of gold transported from South Africa to Britain at the beginning of last year was £1.5 million. However, on September 8th and 15th, it suddenly dropped from £1,054,000 to £353,000, and has not recovered since. However, South Africa has not stopped mining gold. Therefore, it can be seen that the reason why gold is staying in South Africa is probably due to the instructions of the British authorities. In these days of war clouds, it is indeed a good idea to keep a portion of the gold reserves in its own territory for safety reasons.

Recent Gold Reserve Estimates: Three months have passed since this official report was published. In these three months, of course, a large amount of gold has flowed out of Britain. Now, starting from the Exchange Equalization Fund's £152 million on September 30th, let us speculate on the situation of gold outflow after September 30th. First, let's look at the current situation of the import and export of gold in Britain: (Unit: Thousand Pounds)

October to December 1938

Imports Exports

From France 14,028 To the United States 102,984

Belgium 8,340 Canada 3,280

Holland 3,752 Belgium 1,910

Germany 2,570 Eire 1,010

South Africa 1,856 Sweden 978

West Africa 1,668 Switzerland 608

Switzerland 1,610 Others 386

India 1,469

Others 2,304

Total 37,597 Total 111,156

According to the above table, the net export of gold is £73,559,000, but there are still some things to consider. First, in the week before October 6th, £7,661,000 of gold was transported to Britain from Belgium, but this was deposited in London by the Belgian government for safety reasons, so its ownership did not change. On the contrary, it is questionable whether there is any refuge gold included in the £1,910,000 transported to Belgium. If this is taken as an indication of the Belgian people's settlement, then £7,661,000 should be subtracted from the total amount of imports.

Secondly, only £1,856,000 of gold was transported from South Africa. If calculated at £1.5 million per week, there should be £19,500,000. It can be seen that £17,600,000 of British special designated items remained in South Africa in three months. In addition, some of the gold transported to Canada may have been transported by the British authorities for safety reasons, but the amount is unknown.

Based on this, the gold export number can be revised to: (Million Pounds)

Net exports reported 73.6

Plus the import of Belgian refuge gold 7.7

Total 81.3

Minus the estimated number of designated items in South Africa and Canada 18.3

Net loss of the Exchange Equalization Fund 63.0

This amount of only £63 million is not enough to see the whole picture. The settlement purchases in the London gold market can offset this number, because the settlement includes gold imports. However, the situation caused by hoarding purchases is the opposite. After the approval of resale, the Exchange Equalization Fund has supplied £5 million of gold for hoarding in the last three months. In addition, it was also affected by the withdrawal of French gold, which Reynaud estimated to be £34 million, reaching £50 or £60 million by the end of the year. However, those shipped out of London accounted for £30 million.

Although the French Exchange Control has purchased gold pounds today, there is still no record of gold flowing from London into Paris. Some say that this gold pound has been converted into US dollars and has flowed into New York. This is to be expected, but the amount of British gold transferred to French designated items probably does not exceed £5 million at most. Adding the Exchange Equalization Fund's loss in the last three months, estimated at £73 million, then the British Exchange Equalization Fund on December 31, 1938, had only £80 million of gold remaining. (Calculated as an integer)

If calculated at the current market price of 150 shillings per ounce, then £80 million is actually worth £86 million, which can strengthen the technical position of equalizing foreign exchange. The "autumn crisis" has now passed, and most of the "hot money" stored in London has successively flowed out. It is expected that the US dollar will also be sold short, so its price will inevitably rise. As a result, general speculators may turn to need British pounds. In addition, the year-end clearance of the US dollar will enable the Exchange Equalization Fund to have some US dollars or designated gold stored in the United States. This is tantamount to hiding reserves and can recover the gold that the Bank of England sold to the Exchange Equalization Fund at the end of 1936. Recently, the number of trust banknotes issued will recover £30 million, and the extraction of £30 million of gold from the bank's issuing department will reduce its gold reserves by this amount, but the Exchange Equalization Fund will give the bank £30 million of securities. When this gold is transferred to the Exchange Equalization Fund, it can be raised to £53 million, calculated at 150 shillings per ounce. Therefore, the Exchange Equalization Fund's gold reserves will restore the number of £139 million. If there are no major political entanglements in the future, the technical position of the British pound is sufficient to meet general needs.

Wartime Shanghai Financial Market (Continued) 38

— Zhu Boquan

(6) Revival of the Cash Market Shanghai's gold market was originally a place for speculators to operate. In the past, monthly transactions often reached three to four million taels, but after the currency reform, it became deserted, with monthly transactions of only four to five thousand taels. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, it stopped completely. China's monetary system was originally based on silver, but since the implementation of the legal tender policy, it has become a managed currency. The exchange rate with foreign currencies has long lost its connection with the fluctuations of world gold and silver prices. However, since the government implemented foreign exchange controls last March, speculators have once again taken advantage of the fluctuations in the world's gold and silver ratios to manipulate them. As a result, the cash trading in Shanghai's unofficial market has suddenly become active. After May last year, the Shanghai cash price was affected by the London market, and a surge began, rising to 2,000 yuan in mid-June (the standard price for ten taels of gold). It once softened, but then rose again, reaching 2,068 yuan in November. At the beginning of March this year, due to a shortage of cash chips, coupled with purchases from North China, it once created a high price of 2,200 yuan, and is currently hovering around 2,100 yuan. Compared with before the war, it has risen by about 1,000 yuan. Although the cash market can affect the movement of a portion of gold, because China's foreign exchange base has become stable and the Sino-American Silver Agreement was also extended last year, it does not seem to have any impact on the overall financial situation.

(7) Changes in Clearinghouse Transactions Shanghai's clearinghouse transactions are divided into three groups: Chinese banks and money shops, and foreign banks. The Chinese Banks Clearing House was established in January 1933, and is sponsored by the Bankers' Joint Reserve Association. Its clearing procedures are similar to those of European and American countries. Money shops also have an organization called the Exchange Remittance Association, but their clearing methods are very outdated. As for the clearing of instruments between Bund banks (including foreign banks and the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Farmers Bank of China), there is only a reconciliation method and no clearinghouse organization or system.

Before the war, the bank clearinghouse held two clearing sessions every day at 1:00 PM and 3:30 PM. After the war, due to a decrease in instruments, it was changed to once a day at 3:00 PM. From January to July 1937, the average daily clearing amount of the clearinghouse was more than 29 million yuan. From August to December, the daily average was only 7 million yuan, a ratio of about four to one. From January to July 1938, the daily average was only more than 6 million yuan. From August to December, there was a slight improvement, with a daily average of about 9 million yuan. Among the clearing amounts in the months after the war, December 1937 and December 1938 were the lowest, with a daily average of only 3.6 million yuan. However, the clearing amount has gradually increased recently. In January of this year, the daily average clearing amount has reached more than 24 million yuan, almost the same as the daily average before the war, which shows that Shanghai's commercial transactions have gradually become active under special circumstances.

The money shops' clearinghouse transactions are commonly known as "Zha Gong Che." The daily clearing amount includes the amount of interbank lending and transfer accounts, which is different in nature from the bank clearing figures and is difficult to compare. However, general observations show that the trend of the rise and fall of the money shops' clearing amount after the war is the same as that of the bank clearing figures. As for the clearing methods of the money industry, there have been slight improvements after the war. In the past, each money shop sent old cashiers to collect bills separately, but now each money shop sends two clearing staff to the Exchange Remittance Association from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM every day to handle the clearing centrally. In addition, the money shops' interbank clearing bills were originally stipulated that those over 500 yuan should be marked with large public bills, and those under 500 yuan and odd amounts should be marked with small public bills, which were cleared daily at the money industry reserve. In November last year, the Money Industry Association decided to cancel the names of large and small, and all amounts, regardless of the amount, should be marked with one public bill, which should be cleared daily, simplifying the procedures.

As for the clearing procedures of the Bund banks, after verifying the instruments with each other, the Bank of China used large transfer slips for the overall remittance, and the difference was settled daily by means of depositing or withdrawing cash. There was no clearinghouse organization. Since the outbreak of the war, the large transfer slip method adopted in the past has been abandoned, and each bank now sends personnel to the HSBC bank at 11:30 AM every day to conduct centralized verification. In addition, foreign banks have never had deposit and loan relationships with Chinese banks. After the war, for the convenience of clearing, foreign banks exceptionally opened current accounts with our Central Bank, and the Central Bank also opened accounts with foreign banks. As a result, the daily receivables and payables of Chinese and foreign banks are entrusted to each other for collection, and transferred within the current accounts, which is much more convenient than before.

The Situation of the Financial Industry Since the outbreak of the war, the environment in which the Shanghai financial industry is located has been very unusual. Leaving aside foreign banks for the time being, as far as Chinese banks and money shops are concerned, since the July 7th Incident two years ago, there has been a wave of withdrawals. In the month before the outbreak of the Shanghai war, the deposits of various banks and money shops clearly decreased. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, the banking and money industry closed for four days. After the government promulgated measures to stabilize the financial situation, people's hearts began to stabilize slightly, and deposits did not decrease significantly. As the war zone expanded, wealthy people from various places came to Shanghai to seek refuge with their assets. As a result, the deposits of various banks and money shops gradually increased. However, most of these increased deposits were current deposits. On the banking and money industry side, it was necessary to accumulate sufficient reserves to respond to the situation.

After the war, the business policies of various banks and money shops strived for stability, and they were very cautious about various loans, mostly reducing the scope of business, only accepting deposits and not making loans. Fortunately, a portion of the pawnshop customers of the banking and money industry who suffered losses in the war, recently benefited from the high prices in Shanghai. In addition to making up for the losses of the war, they also had surpluses. Therefore, the loans made by the banking and money industry before the war, except for customers who suspended business during the war, could often be recovered on time. In addition, the business of various banks, except for a portion of loans, foreign exchange and other businesses, inevitably stagnated after the war, while other businesses such as warehousing, real estate trusts, etc., have increased compared with before the war. This kind of abnormal development is the only phenomenon in the current special environment in Shanghai, and it is self-evident that it cannot last long.

The loss of assets of the banking and money industry during the war was inevitable. Fortunately, most banks and money shops usually operate stably and have sufficient reserves. The previous surpluses are more than enough to offset the current losses. Only a very small number of smaller banks suffered from the impact of the war, and there were rumors of financial difficulties. As for those who went bankrupt as a result, there was only one bank. At the same time, among the four banks that suspended business in the month before the outbreak of the war, two had resumed business one after another last year.

The four banks of the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Farmers Bank of China are the largest government banks in the country and have outstanding influence in the financial industry. Their head offices were originally located in Shanghai. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, these four government banks moved their head offices to the inland and established branches in various provinces in the southwest and Hong Kong. Shanghai's financial power has become dispersed. Currently, Shanghai's banks feel that the channels and targets for their usual use of funds have been blocked and reduced after the war. In addition, the government is actively promoting and encouraging investment in the development of agriculture, mining, industry, and commerce in the inland. Therefore, general commercial banks in Shanghai have a tendency to develop towards the inland. Recently, many banks have established branches in the provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Guangxi. The center of gravity of finance has shifted, and the future development is worthy of attention.

However, as they are being sent to the original speakers for review, they can only be published in the next issue. Hongqiao Japanese Headquarters Heavily Attacked by Guerrillas 55

Hou's Troops Departing from Panlong, Japanese Aircraft at the Airfield Destroyed

More Than a Dozen Japanese Soldiers Killed, Three Wounded in Hou's Troops

Hou Junren, the leader of the powerful guerrilla forces in western Shanghai, led his troops from Panlong Town yesterday morning when the sky was slightly bright, detouring and advancing towards the Japanese military base in Hongqiao. He surrounded the Japanese military headquarters and launched a fierce attack. Another team of warriors was selected to break into the airfield and destroy a Japanese aircraft. The Japanese army also desperately broke through the encirclement, and the two sides fought for about two hours. Just as the Japanese army was unable to support, the Japanese army from Tushanwan heard the alarm and suddenly dispatched more than 200 security guards to join the battle. Hou was afraid of being outnumbered and falling into a deep encirclement, and the purpose had been achieved, so he led his troops back to their original location. In addition to destroying a Japanese aircraft, more than a dozen Japanese soldiers were killed in this battle, and three warriors were wounded in Hou's troops.

Japanese Army Attacked Xinzhuang and Was Defeated Xinzhuang Town, the fourth station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, is the border between Shanghai and Songjiang, and is connected to the Shanghai-Min Highway. Therefore, for the convenience of controlling and commanding the guerrillas, a headquarters was set up there to carry out mobile warfare in southern and western Shanghai. The Japanese army received a report from a traitor on the morning of the 17th and launched a night attack. Unexpectedly, the guerrillas had already taken precautions and set up an ambush, causing the Japanese army to be surrounded in the village and suddenly collapse, fleeing towards Zhuanqiao in Shanghai County. The guerrillas took advantage of the situation to pursue from both sides. The Japanese army was unable to stand still, so they rushed straight to Hongqiao Road in western Shanghai along the Shanghai-Min Road. At that time, they abandoned a lot of guns, ammunition, and baggage, and the guerrillas gained an unexpected harvest. Yesterday, they began to clear up the fake "self-defense corps" on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road.

Japanese Naval Bombardment of Zha Port Two small Japanese warships, carrying dozens of naval marines, sailed to the vicinity of Zha Port in southern Huangpu and indiscriminately fired cannons at the town. Houses far and near were shaken. More than a dozen residents of the town who did not have time to escape were killed, and all the houses were turned to ashes.

Guerrilla Attack on Dujiagang After several tug-of-war battles, most of the merchants and people in Dujiagang moved away, and it has become a dead market. The guerrillas of the Li Zhiming unit suddenly advanced to the area the night before last (the 17th). The naval marines of the Japanese army stationed there heard the alarm and immediately fired dense guns and cannons at the shore. The Li unit was divided into two units, one attacking the back of the Japanese army and encircling the Japanese army on land, and the other scattered along the coast to resist the Japanese navy. They fought back and forth for one or two hours before the Li unit withdrew to its original defense. After investigation, dozens of Japanese soldiers were killed or wounded, and four members of the Li unit were killed or wounded.

Japanese Army Demolished Houses in Shangchuan The war in the three counties of Pudong, Fengnan, and Chuan has been quite fierce recently. The Japanese army believed that guerrillas were hiding in the houses along the Shangchuan Railway. Yesterday (the 18th), they transferred more than 200 engineers to demolish the houses along the road one after another. When the residents heard the news, they were all panicked.

More than 500 alumni and guests attended, including Yu Qiaqing and Lin Kanghou, who also came to offer their congratulations.

Mr. Ma Xiangbo, the founder of Fudan University, celebrated his centenary birthday yesterday. To express their congratulations, the Fudan Alumni Association of this city held a birthday celebration at the New Asia Restaurant at 6 p.m. There were more than 500 attendees, including guests Yu Qiaqing, Xu Ji, Yuan Ludeng, Lin Kanghou, Yu Zuoting, and alumni in Shanghai Jiang Yiping, Xi Yushu, and Xu Xiaochu, among others. The event was unprecedentedly grand. First, the chairman, Ye Jichun, expressed his gratitude, followed by Jiang Yiping reading a congratulatory message. After the dinner, an annual meeting was held, and the event concluded joyfully at around 10 p.m.

Agenda of the Meeting: (1) Opening; (2) Chairman's Speech; (3) Birthday Greetings; (4) Dinner; (5) Annual Meeting; (A) School Song; (B) Speeches; (C) Report on Association Affairs; (D) Report on the Recent Situation by Representatives of the Alma Mater; (E) Discussion; (F) Entertainment; (G) Raffles; (H) Adjournment.

Chairman's Speech: Chairman Ye Jichun said in his congratulatory speech, "Today is the 100th birthday of Elder Ma Xiang, and the Fudan Alumni Association is holding a celebration in particular. We are deeply honored by the presence of all the guests. Mr. Ma's birthday is the gengzi year of the Daoguang reign, which according to the lunar calendar is February 17th, and according to the Gregorian calendar is March 19th, 1940. Everyone present here today must be very happy. It is rare to hear of someone living to be a hundred years old. We only hear of old people in the countryside who do not ask about worldly affairs and live a life of peace and contentment to reach one hundred years old, but even that is rare. However, Elder Xiang lived to be a hundred years old, and he did not only care for himself. He is always doing things for society. This is truly unprecedented. Perhaps you doubt the words 'unprecedented,' but in China's more than 4,000-year history, although there have been people who lived to be a hundred years old, it is very rare for famous people to live to be a hundred years old. We are now participating in an unprecedented grand event, and we are truly very honored."

Xia Jinguang's Thank You Speech: Xia Jinguang, representing the Ma family, said in his thank you speech, "Today I am very honored to participate in Ma Shou's birthday as a guest. When I met Mr. Ma, he was already in his sixties. At that time, he was running Fudan Public School. I had no experience in education, and Mr. Xiangbo guided me in everything. For the sake of the school, he struggled tirelessly and created today's Fudan, full of talented people, all of whom he cultivated. Today, I am very grateful for everyone's presence and extend my infinite gratitude on behalf of Elder Xiang."

Holding the Annual Meeting: Finally, the alumni association meeting was held, reporting on association affairs, discussing action plans, and adding wonderful entertainment to liven up the atmosphere. In addition, each participant received a pair of longevity bowls, a commemorative medal, and supplies donated by various manufacturers, and everyone was beaming with joy. The event concluded joyfully at around 10 p.m.

Shipping Companies Submit Employee Reports Today: Yesterday, various shipping companies in this city received instructions from the Ningbo Shipping Association, which was forwarded by the Yin County Government, stating that the total number of crew members, buyers, and sailors (including all personnel on board) of each ship sailing on the Shanghai-Ningbo line should be investigated and registered in detail to prevent impersonation and false pretenses. The notice required shipping companies to submit lists of their buyers and sailors, including their names, native places, ages, genders, the months and years they have worked on the ship, their positions, their levels of education, and their home addresses, along with two photos each. These lists should be compiled by the association and submitted to the government for review. The progress of the process should also be reported to the government for record. The association yesterday sent letters to various shipping companies, requesting them to prepare the lists of buyers and sailors, along with two photos each, within five days and submit them to the association for compilation and submission.

Unilaterally Changing Tax Rates Benefits Japan, Hitting British and American Businesses

On the export side, cotton was tax-free, and the tax rates on wool were reduced.

Trade of Various Countries Affected: The trade of Britain, the United States, Germany, and France with China has been sharply reduced since January of the 27th year of the Republic due to the seizure of the customs offices in the occupied areas of China by the Japanese and puppet authorities and the unilateral modification of tax rates. Garages Along the Road 69

Prohibited from Being Converted into Living Rooms

The French Public Works Bureau Formulated Measures

Because the population of Shanghai has increased sharply, the French Concession Public Works Bureau has formulated four regulations on the use of garages, ordering owners to comply, in order to prevent the sub-landlords from building mezzanine floors and using garages for rent. The regulations are copied as follows: Article 1. It is strictly forbidden to use garages along the road as living rooms, workshops, shops, or warehouses. However, this rule does not apply to those who have applied to the French Public Works Bureau and have been approved. Article 2. All applications should be reviewed by the Board of Directors of the French Public Works Bureau and submitted to the Consul General for a decision. Article 3. The above permission is not of a permanent nature. If its neighbors or the Director General of the French Police Department raise reasonable objections, the Board of Directors of the French Public Works Bureau may adopt the opinions and revoke the permission at any time. Article 4. Anyone who violates these regulations shall be fined from five to one hundred yuan, and those living in the garage may be ordered to move out by the police station.

Large Shipment of Quinine to China; Gift from the American Red Cross to Refugees 71

Anticipating Severe Malaria Epidemic This Summer; To Be Unloaded in Hong Kong

The Continental Daily reports that a member of the American Advisory Committee in Shanghai told reporters yesterday (the 18th) that the American Red Cross has donated two million tablets of quinine to Chinese refugees, which have now been shipped to China. He believes that the Chinese Red Cross, which is actively fighting malaria and other diseases in the mainland, has appealed for donations of medicines. The committee member explained that due to the influx of refugees suffering from malaria into the mainland, the disease is rapidly spreading from one area to another. Therefore, a severe malaria epidemic is expected this summer. To distinguish the medicine, all tablets are colored blue. The boxes are also labeled to indicate that the tablets inside are donated by the American Red Cross. They will be unloaded in Hong Kong and then transported to the mainland by the Chinese Red Cross. As for the crushed wheat recently shipped to China by the American Red Cross, there are still about nine thousand bags left here. Chinese refugees enjoy eating it, and even the poor people in South China who are accustomed to eating rice have repeatedly requested continued donations.

North-Sha Route Extremely Prosperous 72

Chinese Troops Stationed at Various Ports; Foreign Ships Sail Frequently

The inland ports in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River have been under Japanese control. Regulations stipulate that foreign ships must obtain navigation permits before sailing. Most foreign merchants refuse to cooperate and have announced the suspension of navigation. Inland merchants have also ceased doing business due to the Japanese puppet regime's control over exports, requiring export permits, and the illegal collection of taxes at various ports, which are unbearable. They have switched to transporting goods through ports stationed by Chinese troops. Therefore, ports such as Beisha, Songji Port, Sanhe Port, Hutong Port, Niuhong Port, Shuji Port, Da'an Port, Laohong Port, Xingang Port, Lingxun Port, and Dongyi Port, which are still under the control of the puppet guerrillas, have become the central points for the transfer of inland cargo. Foreign shipping companies have dispatched ships to sail frequently. According to investigations, there are more than ten foreign ships sailing, including Yihe, Tonghe, Deyao, Daxin, Lisha, Haiyi, Sanbei, and Hongyun, with five or six ships traveling back and forth daily. The Beisha route has now become the most prosperous route in the inland ports. Although the Xingang route is still operating as usual, the number of passenger and freight ships has sharply decreased, with only seven or eight ships sailing.

Shanghai Refugee Relief Association (Continued) (Yesterday) Policies on Managing Shelters 74

It must be understood that refugees are not slaves, let alone prisoners. Refugees are people who have suffered during national crises, a general term for those who have suffered within war zones. The only difference is that there are refugees in shelters, refugees not in shelters, and even refugees like us serving in refugee shelters. Everyone must understand that refugees in shelters are not a different kind of people, but compatriots who stand in the same position as us. Therefore, the enthusiastic donations of people from all walks of life and our service to the majority of refugees are all about fulfilling our mutual assistance obligations. Even Westerners are doing their best to help us, let alone our own people.

Some things are heavier than Mount Tai, and some are lighter than a feather. The resignation of Mr. Cai and Mr. Wang a few days ago was indeed justifiable. The future work is indeed more important than the positions they resigned from. Moreover, both gentlemen had stated before coming here to work that they were only helping out temporarily. Therefore, the farewell ceremony was very grand, not only to respect the two gentlemen but also to encourage colleagues to work hard. Unexpectedly, after Cai and Wang, anyone who has other work immediately resigns, regardless of whether they are responsible or whether someone else can take over. Now there is Zhang Yiyi, who, while serving in the shelter, was reprimanded and recorded for abusing refugees and disobeying the director's orders after investigation. Last night, he left without permission and went to other places. The contents of the letter he left behind are even more unreasonable. Such irresponsibility and disobedience will not lead to good results even if he works elsewhere. His unpaid monthly salary will be used as a donation to refugees as a warning to others. If anyone still intends to resign and take on other tasks, you must declare it today so that we can prepare for replacements as soon as possible. Otherwise, I cannot leave my job without permission. You must know that this shelter is not a place for you to rest temporarily, so we cannot allow you to come and go as you please.

Let's talk about the meager treatment first. As far as I know, compared with other shelters, our association is still relatively high. Those of you who have served in other shelters must know that. As for the work of collecting badges and numbering refugees, it must be completed within two days. Deliver it to Mr. Chen Yuze of the Standard Company to make it, distribute and hang it, so that the photos of the adopted refugees can also be completed as soon as possible (to be continued).

arrest at that time, as well as the confessions of the defendants at the police station. Father Chops Off Leg Bones of Sick Child 83

Eleven Born, All Completely Dead; Chopping Off Leg Bones So They Won't Be Reincarnated; Police Station Prosecutes for Murder

Cai Heshang (49 years old) and Cai Xu (48 years old), a couple from Jiangbei who live at No. 108, Alley 87, Kangnaot Road, chopped off the leg bones of their sick baby Cai Xiaoya (their own daughter, only 56 days old) with an ax on the open space behind the public toilet of the Shanghai Municipal Council near Wuding Road, Tokyo Road, at 3 pm on the 13th of this month. She died of her injuries and was arrested by the Gordon Road Police Station. Yesterday, they were prosecuted by the First Special Court for murder under Article 271, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Judge Huang Risheng took the seat to hear the case. The defendant Cai Heshang confessed, "I make a living as a rickshaw puller. Including the daughter who died now, I have given birth to eleven children in total, and none of them survived. We have a superstition in our hometown that children who cannot be raised are 'debt collectors.' If you don't use harsh methods against them, they will still be reincarnated. This child was only fifty days old when she was born, and she was sick. She saw a doctor every day. On the afternoon of the 13th, she died again. My wife was holding her in her arms and crying. I was very angry, so I took the body of this 'debt collector' to the open space on Tokyo Road and chopped off her right leg bone with an ax. Who would have thought that when I chopped down with an ax, she came back to life and was calling. I was very scared in my heart, suspecting that the 'debt collector' was showing up. I threw the ax at her body and ran back." At this point in the interrogation, the court turned to Cai Xu for questioning. The defendant was then ordered to be returned to custody, and the case was scheduled for re-interrogation on the 25th of this month when the autopsy report arrived.

The Gu Zhuxuan Case Has Been Suspended

Declaration of Innocence, expressed dissatisfaction and submitted a petition to the Third High Branch Court's Prosecutor's Office, requesting that they appeal to the Supreme Court on their behalf, seeking to punish Gu with the crime he deserved. Further Questioning. Quentin Roosevelt Comes to China to Search for the Golden Monkey of Tibet and Collect Other Animal Specimens 85

According to the Continental News, Quentin Roosevelt, the son of Mr. and Mrs. Theodore Roosevelt, arrived in Shanghai by plane from Japan yesterday (the 18th). He will travel to Kunming and then Dali on Tuesday before entering Tibet to search for the golden monkey of western China and Tibet, as well as other animal specimens unique to the area. When interviewed by reporters yesterday, he stated that he was traveling alone and that all the materials he obtained would be displayed in the Boston Museum of Fine Arts and two other museums, which are funding his trip. In addition to collecting animal specimens, he will also study the uncivilized ethnic groups of western China. He expects to return to Shanghai around the end of June. Mr. Roosevelt graduated from Harvard University and came to Shanghai with his mother during the war in 1937. His parents are also planning a trip to the Far East this year and may arrive in Shanghai before the end of June to welcome their son's return from his long journey.

Gambling Den Owner Loses Money and Resorts to Infighting, Opening Fire 86

Gao Jingen, a 34-year-old native of Suzhou, residing at No. 64 Yong'an Lane, Difeng Road, in western Shanghai, was very friendly with Mr. Wang, the owner of the "Yongyuan Company" gambling den near Caojiadu. Before the den opened, Mr. Wang lacked capital, and Gao, due to his active involvement in illicit activities around Yong'an Lane, had some savings. Therefore, Wang persuaded Gao to become a partner. In addition, Gao lent Wang 700 yuan as Wang's capital. Unexpectedly, after the den opened, business was poor. Recently, due to the Huajun Special Operations Team actively cracking down and warning various gambling dens and opium dens to close down quickly or face punishment, most gamblers hesitated to visit, and the gambling dens became desolate, plummeting in business. The Yongyuan gambling den was particularly deserted and declining. Gao Jingen, witnessing his investment possibly becoming worthless, became anxious and went to Yongyuan around 7:00 PM yesterday to demand repayment of the loan from Wang. However, Wang denied it, claiming that the money was Gao's share of the capital. This led to a dispute between the two, and they roared at each other in the den's accounting room, refusing to yield. Unable to reach an agreement, they resorted to violence. Mr. Wang, seized by murderous intent, took out a concealed handgun and fired six shots at Gao. Fortunately, Gao dodged effectively and was only hit once in the right arm, allowing him to escape. However, still indignant, he reported the incident to the Concession police, who dispatched Chinese police officer No. 252 to send him to the hospital for treatment and to investigate the truth and pursue the culprit.

To the Esteemed Editor, We are writing in response to a statement from our client, Ms. Zheng Songliangzhao, who has read the news article titled "Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law as Strangers: Elderly Woman Sues for Support" in your newspaper on January 15th. The article stated that Ms. Zheng has always had disagreements with her mother-in-law, Ms. Cheng, so Ms. Cheng, now over seventy years old, still lives separately at No. 74 Hengmao Lane, Baxianqiao. Not only are the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law like strangers, but the three grandsons, following their mother's instructions, also do not know to offer filial piety. It also claimed that the daughter-in-law is wealthy but never provides any assistance. This is inconsistent with the facts. Ms. Zheng and her mother-in-law, Ms. Cheng, have always been harmonious. Since Ms. Cheng moved to Shanghai, eight years have passed. Besides personally visiting Ms. Cheng to inquire about her well-being, she has also instructed her children to visit their grandmother regularly to provide care. The claim of long-standing disagreements is not factual. Furthermore, after the death of the late Mr. Shunian, the land rent he left behind, besides the 196 piculs taken by Ms. Cheng as sustenance, included more than 200 piculs that were inherited and benefited from by Mr. Gongwu, Ms. Zheng's husband. After her husband's death, she has been living on this income. The expenses for daily necessities, food, clothing, and the children's education have been extremely difficult to manage. As for the inherited shops, most of them have experienced poor business after her husband inherited them and have closed down one after another within a year, resulting in no income. During this time of national crisis, rent collection has decreased, and the hardship is beyond description. Moreover, in mid-November of last winter, she jointly withdrew 14 mu of farmland from the safety deposit box with Ms. Cheng as a mortgage for 1,000 yuan for Ms. Cheng. The claim that the daughter-in-law is wealthy but never provides any assistance is also inconsistent with the facts. Therefore, we have been specially entrusted by your lawyer to make corrections in order to set the record straight. We hereby respectfully request that you publish this letter in the Letters to the Editor section. Sincerely, Attorney Peng Zhongjun, March 18th.

Talks

Promoting the Children's One-Cent Donation Campaign 92

— Yucai

There are still 100,000 refugees in Shanghai. These 100,000 refugees rely on the efforts of the Refugee Relief Association to solicit donations to maintain their lives. Almost everyone knows and appreciates the Refugee Relief Association. But can the association itself succeed? It cannot succeed. The association is empty. Its success depends entirely on the enthusiastic donations of people from all walks of life in Shanghai. It requires all the people of Shanghai, with one heart and one mind, to contribute money and effort, and to care about the lives of the displaced. Only in this way can the association succeed. When we look at the association's published income and expenditure reports in the newspaper, we can see that the amount of donations is quite considerable. However, because there are so many people who need relief, the distribution is not very generous. The future is long, and how will it continue? This is a problem. The refugees are all our dear compatriots, and we should all stand up and take responsibility to solve their living problems.

April 4th is Children's Day, an annual event. This year is the eighth. In the past, there were grand celebrations every Children's Day. The Children's Day this year has also been initiated and prepared by various children's education organizations. I personally believe that the celebration ceremony can be simple, but we should take this opportunity to promote thrift and promote a one-cent relief campaign. Speaking of this, some people may misunderstand that the donations in schools are too heavy. Sometimes there is a one-yuan charity donation, sometimes there is a thrift and relief donation, and sometimes there is a one-cent relief donation. The economic conditions of the children are very ordinary. Where do they have so much surplus money? This sounds very good on the surface, but it is wrong after careful analysis. The one-yuan charity donation is only once. It is used as a production education fund for the displaced, and it is not necessarily forced to donate. The total number of students in all large, medium, and small schools in Shanghai is about 300,000, but the goal is only set at 100,000 yuan. This means that some of the poorer students are expected to be exempt from donating. Moreover, it is now the end of the result, and there will be no more one-yuan charity donations in the future. Thrift and relief donations and one-cent relief donations are two sides of the same coin, but the one-cent relief donation is more specific. It is not very difficult for a child to save one cent a day. We only need to look at the business situation of consumer cooperatives in many schools to see that children are fully capable of contributing a one-cent donation. Donating one cent per person per day is three cents per month. Thinking of the last time the citizens' group launched a fundraising campaign to adopt displaced people, knowing that donating two yuan per month can save one person's monthly living expenses, wouldn't two children be able to save one displaced person? "Many grains of sand make a tower, and many fox furs make a robe." This is absolutely correct. It looks like it is only one cent, but the effect is very great. Children of Shanghai, I believe you are all enthusiastic. Starting today, implement a one-cent donation campaign. 100,000 displaced people are eagerly expecting you.

Life Photo

The Words of a Newspaper Vendor (Continued) 93

— Yuan Xiangsheng, Tenth Newspaper Vendor School

After getting the newspapers, I hurry to the bus stop on Connaught Road and Xiaoshadu Road to sell them. At that time, many gentlemen who worked in offices went to work, so business was not bad. However, sometimes it is inevitable that you will not be able to sell them all. When they are about to be sold out, you have to deliver the newspapers to the homes of subscribers. Your feet do not allow you to be lazy at all. What newspaper vendors hate the most is rainy days. Sometimes the weather is very good when you leave home. Unfortunately, when you get the newspapers to sell, it starts to rain heavily. You don't have an umbrella, so you undo the buttons on your body and put the newspapers in your chest. The ruthless raindrops hit you, and you are drenched all over. It is very uncomfortable. A weak body may catch a cold and get sick. If you walk faster on a rainy road, there is a real danger of slipping and falling. Therefore, it is inevitable that the time for delivering newspapers will be delayed. If you meet a good subscriber, they won't say anything. However, some impatient gentlemen will ask why the newspapers were delivered so late. They can't know the reason and the reason why several newspaper offices publish late. Really, sometimes the newspaper offices have to wait for news or other reasons until very late before they publish. This makes the newspaper vendors suffer. Not only do they have to run like a race on the road, but they also have to be blamed by the subscribers. Therefore, I think it would be good if the newspaper offices could publish the newspapers before 7:00 AM, because some subscribers don't know the reason why we deliver the newspapers late and think that the newspaper vendors are lazy. Because we are short of time, we don't have time to explain in detail, so we have to vaguely say that we will deliver them earlier tomorrow.

After delivering all the newspapers to the subscribers, your feet can finally get a chance to rest. The whole morning is spent in a hurry. It can also be said that you have spent a day as a newspaper vendor.

But there are also those who sell the evening newspapers together. Of course, you can earn more money, but you have to work harder physically. Newspaper vendors with large families have to work harder to maintain their family life. (The End)

Talking about Czechoslovakia 94

— Reflection

Czechoslovakia has been established for twenty years. During the First European War, thanks to the leadership of Masaryk and the courageous struggle of the people, Czechoslovakia was created. It was really not easy. As a result of twenty years of hard work, Czechoslovakia can also be called a powerful country. Its industrial development and exquisite military industry are especially praised by the world. Therefore, when Czechoslovakia is mentioned, people immediately think of its products. Its prevalence can be imagined.

Czechoslovakia has a population of 14 million and a land area of 140,000 kilometers. It is a very small country. Its location is between Germany, Hungary, Poland, Romania, and other countries. It borders the strong neighbor Germany and is adjacent to Hungary, Romania, Poland, and other countries. Therefore, the prosperity of Czechoslovakia could have increased the courage of small and weak nations. However, it is inevitable that it will be envied by strong neighbors. When Germany and Italy tried every means to expand their power in Europe, Czechoslovakia had already been considered a piece of fat. In addition to the fact that many lands were ceded to Germany, Hungary, and Poland last year, the problem of the declaration of independence by the Slovak Province and the Carpathian Ukraine Province has caused disintegration. The remaining provinces of Bohemia and Moravia have been occupied by Germany, so Czechoslovakia has been broken and fallen.

This incident originated from the disputes between the Slavic ethnic group and the Czech ethnic group. There are many Slavic ethnic groups living in the Slovak Province of Czechoslovakia. This ethnic group and the soldiers' living habits are incompatible, and conflicts often occur. After Germany annexed the Sudetenland, it helped the Slavic ethnic group to carry out an independence movement in Czechoslovakia, wanting to first make the Slavic Province and Carpathian Province become German vassals, and continue to pave the way for the eastward advance and attack the Soviet Union. Unexpectedly, the facts were beyond expectations. Under German pressure, Czechoslovakia allowed the Slovak Province and the Carpathian Province to become independent, and even asked Germany to protect the provinces of Bohemia and Moravia. Therefore, the provinces of Bohemia and Moravia were immediately allowed to be driven straight in by the German army and declared dissolution. When the news came, the world was shocked.

Czechoslovakia has fallen, but the fall of Czechoslovakia did not fire a shot or spend a bullet, which is sad. We believe that the fall of Czechoslovakia was due to Britain and France, because the British and French governments repeatedly tolerated aggression in order to seek temporary peace, which made Czechoslovakia unable to recover. It not only fueled the arrogance of fascism, but also backfired, harming others and not benefiting themselves. It is really a pity. But Czechoslovakia itself is also to blame for not adhering to its own position and relying on others to mediate. If Czechoslovakia had taken the initiative to strengthen its spirit, unite the people, and fight to the death before the Four-Power Conference, the result would not necessarily have been the fall of the country. Even if it was defeated and destroyed, it would have paid a considerable price, which would have been more colorful compared to the current situation of swallowing its breath. Moreover, the war might not have led to the destruction of the country.

Scientific Experiment

An Interesting Toy 95

— Xiaohong

Now let me introduce an interesting toy. This toy is not my creation. It is extracted from books. However, this toy is related to optics. Understanding the mystery of it can let us know the mystery of light and vision. Although it is not an important thing, it is just a toy, but it contains scientific truth. Readers may wish to study it carefully.

Cut a small round piece of cardboard, about two inches wide and three inches long, and draw an object on each side. For example, draw a birdcage on the front of the paper and a bird on the back, and then tie a string to each side of the round paper. Now use your fingers to twist the string to make the round paper rotate rapidly, and the bird will be seen in the cage (see figure). This experiment is very interesting. If students are interested, they can do it according to this. Not only can it be used as a toy, but it can also arouse students' interest in research. It is also strange that it is clearly a bird on one side and a cage on the other. The two are unrelated things. After a few degrees of movement, the bird will get into the cage. Isn't it a strange thing? However, if you study its reason, it is not difficult to discover its scientific mystery, because when we usually look at things with our eyes, the image of the object is reflected on the retina of our eyeballs. At this time, if you suddenly move the object away, the image does not disappear immediately, but can be temporarily retained on the retina. This phenomenon is called "afterimage" in science. When the paper is rotating, the cage image that remains on our retina has not had time to disappear, and the bird image is immediately reflected on the retina, so the result is that the two are superimposed, and we see it as if the bird is in the cage.

Readers can now know the general idea of the above experiment. This is originally a very ordinary thing. An ordinary card is drawn according to the method and then turned to persuade it to work. But the reason is to use the afterimage effect of the retina of our eyeballs to get a continuous illusion. In this way, it seems that there is nothing unusual, but I don't know that scientists often get higher achievements in ordinary experiments. This is what ordinary people cannot do. Ordinary people are indifferent to things, but scientists study to the end. Ordinary people understand a thing, and they consider it done. Scientists understand a thing, and they also use it carefully. For example, an ordinary experiment above, scientists have invented movies based on the "afterimage" effect of people's eyeballs. In this way, it is still the ancestor of movies!

We may have all seen movies. The movement of movies is agile. It can make many fixed human images on the film move. The reason for this is, as we said before, due to the continuous movement, the bird enters the cage. Gentlemen, please think about it. Of course, it will not be different: the movie can be regarded as the largest industry in the modern era. The amount of capital invested and the people who depend on it directly and indirectly make people speechless when they are counted. Not only that, the cultural dissemination effect of movies can also be said to be a unique weapon. It can make things come alive in front of you. It is much better than the teaching method of us sitting stiffly in the classroom and listening to the teacher's lectures. However, its origin is the thing that is not worth a smile mentioned above.

From this, we can also know that we should carefully experience and study the things we encounter in our daily life. Even a very small thing that is not worth looking at should be studied. Although we do not have to become scientists or inventors, it is not useless to study things and use things. I hope readers do not think my words are false.

I am a Refugee 96

— Refugee Reporter

People call me "refugee," and I myself admit that I am a "refugee."

"Refugee" is not a shameful term. It is only because my hometown has been destroyed by war that I have also sacrificed for the country and become a refugee. If my hometown is fortunately not in the war zone, but compatriots from other war zones flee to my hometown, then not only am I not a refugee, I may also be one of those who provide relief to refugees!

Even so, I cannot always rely on the relief of my compatriots. I must learn productive skills and study hard when I have the opportunity to receive an education. Because "refugee" is certainly not a shameful term, but it is shameful to be a "refugee" for the rest of my life!

General Knowledge

The Threshold of Reading Newspapers (I) 99

— Tantian

The old man I know, if I don’t see him for two or three days, when I run into him, he always asks me, “Sir, what’s been happening in the newspaper these days?” So I usually talk to him about the news of the day in general terms and then leave. But when I think about it carefully, the old man knows quite a few characters, and his level of Chinese is really up to the level of a first-year junior high school student, but he often says that he can’t understand the newspaper, he doesn’t understand the threshold. Every time he meets me, he always asks me “What’s been happening in the newspaper?” His meaning seems to be that the newspaper is creating the news, rather than that the society is creating the news. The "Lugou Bridge Incident", the "August 13th Incident", and all the current war news, all happened in the newspaper, rather than actually unfolding around us. This is really a joke!

But there are countless people like him who work hard for a living every day and know a few words but can't understand the newspaper! Moreover, current affairs have a great impact on their lives. For example, why can’t he do business as before the war, and be unemployed? Why are some people moving from the front building to the attic? Why are ordinary people worried about the current high prices? All these current events are directly related to him, so he can't help but care about current events. And he always asks me, "What's been happening in the newspaper?" Alas, in this turbulent era, if people don't understand current affairs, not to mention being unemployed, even people who have jobs, it is very important, because the newspaper not only tells him the necessary social phenomena of the future, but also indicates the actual living conditions of the present. If a person wants to know how to make a living and the steps of being a person, then he must read the newspaper!

Speaking of which, it is not easy for an ordinary person, even if his Chinese foundation is better, to really understand a newspaper. First, when you open a newspaper, your eyes are full of news, and the pages are seven or eight sheets long. Which news is important, is essential to read, which news is secondary, can be omitted. If you read it from beginning to end word for word, there is not so much time. How to start with the Twenty-Four Histories? Second, the layout and style of the news are novel, and the newspaper offices compete to be original. Often the beginning and end are separated, the length is uneven, it looks neither as clear as the Thousand Character Classic nor as easy to understand as Seven Heroes and Five Gallants, often the dragon sees its head but not its tail, making it inexplicable. Third, now science is advancing, culture is developing, and new terms are emerging one after another, some from physics, some from chemistry, and even more from political economy. These terms are naturally not understood by ordinary people. Fourth, the current newspapers, the sources of news, mostly have backgrounds, and are all government propaganda organs, not necessarily standing in the position of the common people to speak, to redress grievances for the common people, and to guide the common people to a way out, so the news published in the newspapers often differs greatly from the facts. Sometimes a major event occurs, and the news in each newspaper is also different. For example, take the "September 18th Incident". Chinese newspapers said that Japan invaded Chinese territory, wanted to destroy China, and dominate Asia. European and American newspapers said that the Japanese army wanted to hinder the interests of the great powers in China and would cause a second world war between the great powers, but Japanese newspapers said that they wanted to maintain peace in East Asia. This kind of statement is similar to Italy's invasion of Abyssinia. The newspapers said that Abyssinia was a barbaric country, and Italy had to civilize Abyssinia for the sake of promoting civilization. From this point of view, there are several ways of saying one thing. The public says the public is right, the wife says the wife is right, and the common people, when they see it, no wonder they don't understand the mystery.

I think, "To enable people like the old man to automatically read the newspaper, we must tell him the threshold of reading the newspaper, so that they first understand the threshold, and then various difficult problems will naturally be solved slowly. This is the best way: However, I myself am not very proficient in the threshold of reading newspapers on weekdays, especially what new terms, the political and economic relations of various countries... etc. I am ashamed to say that I myself do not understand many problems. (To be continued)

Weekly War Report 100

Hubei

The Japanese army in central Hubei, since capturing Zhongxiang last week, is now trying to continue its advance. In recent days, due to the fierce counterattack of the Chinese army, the Japanese army's offensive has become the end of its rope. The Chinese army is actively operating in Changshou Store, Yangzi Town, Shuilong River, and Xiantao Town, which have been successively recovered. The Japanese suffered heavy losses. In addition, the Chinese army once recovered Taipingchang, Chenjiayan, Renjiaji, Yanmenkou and other places, but due to the large number of Japanese troops and the use of gas, they temporarily withdrew. Now the Japanese army is confined to the east bank of the Xiang River, occasionally firing artillery towards the west bank, probably with the intention of holding on. Last week, the Japanese army once again advanced west of Yujia Store, but after being met by the Chinese army, it retreated. There is no action yet. The Chinese army in southern Hubei has repeatedly encountered the Japanese army, especially the battle at the junction of Yangxin and Daye was the fiercest.

Guangdong

The Japanese army in the southern suburbs of Guangdong has recently built fortifications to hold on. The Japanese army occupying Dagang Maoer Ridge was fiercely attacked by Chinese artillery, and the Japanese army seemed to have suffered losses. Afterwards, the Japanese army retreated, and the area was recovered. The Japanese army between Zengcheng and Conghua once advanced towards Taizikeng Zhengguo area to test the waters, while another part of the Japanese army harassed Xiagangling. The Chinese army had sufficient forces and resisted separately, and as a result, the Japanese army failed to succeed. The Chinese army in Huaxian suddenly launched an attack a few days ago, and joined forces with another part of the Chinese army to attack the Japanese army near Changgang. On the same day, Chinese planes flew to Xinjie Taipingchang and other places to bomb, and the Japanese troops in both places suffered losses. In addition, the Chinese army in Hainan Island once launched a fierce attack on the Japanese army in Longmen City, Ding'an County, and Dongxi Township, Qiongshan County. It is said that in this battle, the Japanese army suffered extremely heavy losses and was very angry. They burned and killed wantonly in the city, and the people were disturbed and extremely panicked.

Jiangsu

In Jiangsu Province, the Chinese and Japanese armies have fought fiercely in Huaiyin and Yingcheng since last week. After the strategic shift, the Chinese army actively counterattacked this week in coordination with the large army, and at the same time launched a large-scale guerrilla team to engage in guerrilla warfare. As a result of the fierce battle, Yingcheng has been recaptured by the Chinese army, and Huaiyin is also surrounded by the Chinese army. The Japanese army in Yangzhou once invaded north of Zhaoguan Dam, attempting to threaten the rear of the Chinese army. After the Chinese army skillfully responded, it recaptured Zhaoguan, and the Chinese army is still in hot pursuit.
