Free Talk

The Value of "Non-Recognitionism" 101

— Maolie

Abyssinia was annexed by Italy, and the Italian King was called the Emperor of Abyssinia. The British and French countries initially did not recognize it, but after several twists and turns, they all recognized it one after another. Mussolini's arrogance greatly increased, so he actively assisted Franco, resulting in the victory of the National Army. Sure enough, Britain and France also did not recognize the National Army government at first, but now they have recognized it.

Austria was annexed by Germany. In order to appease the people, Britain and France feared that recognition would be too slow. Hitler's arrogance also greatly increased, so he painstakingly planned and then acted. A few days ago, he again carried out the trick of annexing Bohemia and Moravia, and dividing Czechoslovakia. Britain and France are now playing the non-recognition game again. How long this game will last is still unknown, but it seems to be very short-lived.

Upon investigation, the originator of "non-recognitionism" was Stimson of the United States. At that time, when our country's Northeast was invaded, Stimson had the intention of uniting with Britain to intervene, but Britain refused. Stimson then declared that he would not recognize the changes caused by force, thinking it was a remedy. This non-recognition is still valid!

Of course, with the non-recognition of various countries, at least aggressors can be sanctioned morally, so that aggressors have some scruples, fear, and dare not do whatever they want. This is the value of non-recognitionism. However, the same non-recognition, why does it fail for Abyssinia, Spain, Austria, or even Czechoslovakia, but it can still be effective for China? There is no other reason for this. First, the United States has the determination to maintain morality, and is not swayed by the reality of the violent. Before she has not changed her attitude towards China, other countries do not dare to take the risk of defying the world's justice, and arbitrarily recognize the evil forces of the aggressor; Second, and especially important, I think it is our persistent non-surrender, resisting to the end, which has provided a strong backing for this doctrine.

Therefore, I can say that "non-recognitionism" itself is valuable; But the existence of this value still requires countries that uphold justice to maintain it consistently, and the invaded country must work hard to be self-reliant, and not disappoint the good intentions of those who abide by this doctrine.

Czechoslovakia is finished, and the declaration of non-recognition by Britain and France is just a kind of self-deprecation. Only China is still resisting. Non-recognitionism was originally initiated for the Chinese incident, but its value still needs China to maintain it. China has made this contribution to a legitimate doctrine in the international community, and China is also worthy of pride!

Writing and Personality 102

— GaoGao

Qin Hui and Yan Song committed the crime of slandering loyal ministers and harming the country and the people. Even their pearl-like articles were sentenced to capital punishment and could not be "hidden in famous mountains and passed on to future generations." Zhou Zuoren, in Peiping, was suspected of being a traitor in his behavior. Many secondary schools in Shanghai removed his works from Chinese textbooks, although his personality has not yet reached the period of "assessment."

If the saying "a gentleman does not abandon words because of the person" is credible, I would feel sorry for the people of ancient and modern times. Judging articles by articles, the masterpieces of Qin Hui and Yan Song, "I cannot see them!" I have always held a "high mountain looking up" heart for Zhou Zuoren's articles. To this day, I still hope that he can prove his pure personality with strong facts!

Because of deviant behavior and vile personality, the article is implicated. The general public's view is that it is a kind of punishment, and his spiritual property is completely denied, causing him to suffer deeper pain, whether he is dead or alive. At the same time, it also implies the meaning of killing a chicken to show the monkey, so that scholars who can write do not dare to follow in his footsteps.

Actually, it is not so. Art cannot be separated from life, and works are entrusted to personality. Painting, sculpture, music, all are like this, and literature is especially obvious. It must exist in the heart before it can be expressed externally; it must have a heart that "cannot bear to see people suffer" before it can write the supreme article in the world. Han Yu said: "The so-called writing must have it in the heart. Therefore, a gentleman is cautious in reality. The beauty and ugliness of reality, its expression is not reckless." Tolstoy directly believed that art must be "for life," or even not limited to art. He said: "The prerequisite for all faithful professions is not the love of work, but the love of humanity that must be loved. Under the belief that this work improves humanity, work must be loved. Only those who fill their love with this can do valuable work." Just think, this kindness and harmony, this loyalty and enthusiasm are enough to illuminate the ages; and what about adding sharp eyes, trans-era insights, and artistic skills to express it in writing? Naturally, there is an incredible power. With this power, it arouses the resonance of mankind; with this power, it promotes the reform of politics, law, morality, and thought; with this power, it saves all living beings from deep water and scorching fire. Tolstoy is Tolstoy because of this, and similarly, Gorky is Gorky, Romain Rolland is Romain Rolland, Confucius is Confucius, Pitt is Pitt, Han Yu is Han Yu... also because of this. Then, know that establishing words must be based on establishing virtue, "hiding it in famous mountains and passing it on to future generations" is not something that can be achieved by luck.

What is most taboo in art is hypocritical expression. If you don't drink, you have to compose a few poems about drinking, wild drinking, and expressing your feelings after being drunk; if you are extremely enthusiastic, you have to play the high-profile tune of swearing alliances with seagulls and visiting fishermen and woodcutters; if your chest is full of selfish desires and evil thoughts, you have to say high-sounding words such as taking on righteousness and saving the people. "If you don't establish sincerity in rhetoric," where will there be good writing! Even if you "write as much as your height," it is just a temporary addition of many imitations, many rocks in the universe, not pearls and jade, and you will never be able to pass them on to future generations.

Even if his writing skills are very high, he can cover up the eyes of all people in the world; but his hypocritical life will always be exposed one day, especially in the "cold season." Once exposed, the "insincere" article, the "moment of expensive paper in Luoyang" has passed, and it is still not worth half a penny, for people to "cover the jar." No matter how similar the Yue Fei played on the stage is, he cannot be referred to as a national hero.

I deeply hope that young people who aspire to literature and art, in addition to devoting themselves to the cultivation of skills, will devote themselves to the cultivation of a great personality and a fulfilling life. Write the most sincere and emotional article with kindness, harmony, loyalty and enthusiasm, for yourself who is not in vain in this life, and for the Chinese nation who is resisting the war and building the country!

"Hu Dahai" 103

— Jing Shusen

When it comes to "Hu Dahai," who doesn't know him within a hundred miles? Even the crazy yellow animals have to call him "Sir"!

Speaking of "Hu Dahai's" qualifications, he has also recited the Four Books and read the Five Classics; but he would interpret the words "national tax" as "the country is weakening, so it wants the people to donate money." He would also interpret the sentence "Yan Yuan died, and the Master cried bitterly" in the Analects as "After Yan Yuan died, Confucius cried so much that he wanted to drill a hole." There is no telling how many jokes he has made like this.

Originally, the name "Hu Dahai" was a nickname given to him by others; however, judging by the name, you can know what kind of form and personality he is. Perhaps the enemy thinks he is a bit silly, but somehow, he was appreciated by a general named Teng, who insisted on making him an official and gave him the title of Transportation Minister;—in fact, he was just using him as a handyman to guard the highway and the foreign bridge—and gave him a flag and an armband. The flag was also written with seven big characters: "Hu Dahai, Honorable Sir."

Usually, "Hu Dahai" seems to be there or not; however, after being promoted by General Teng, everyone unanimously said that "Hu Dahai" has officially become a traitor. But "Hu Dahai" does not argue with people.

Once, suddenly "Hu Dahai" happily walked into his home—Luoyang Village—with a fully armed enemy, scaring the people in the village to run around in a panic; especially the young women.

At that time, the people in the village were gnashing their teeth and cursing "Hu Dahai," why didn't he have fun on the street and lead people to the countryside to make trouble? Isn't this "inviting ghosts into the house"!

Hey! This time, "Hu Dahai" did something that no one could have imagined, which was better than eloquent facts: it was not "inviting ghosts into the house," it was clearly "closing the door to catch ghosts"!

It turned out that "Hu Dahai" had repeatedly seen the patrolling enemies slaughtering his compatriots and trampling on the women of his country, and he had long been unable to bear it; however, under the iron hoof, he had no chance to strike. This time, he was waiting for the opportunity: he tricked the most bastard of them into his own home, kindly serving him wine and food; he also called his own wife out to persuade him to drink, slowly getting the bastard drunk, and then seized the weapon that he used to kill people and killed him! This is called "using his own way to treat his own person."

Afterwards, every night, there were always enemies' companions shouting "Boss! Boss..." near Luoyang Village. This is probably the name of the enemy killed by "Hu Dahai," right?

From then on, the flag of "Hu Dahai, Honorable Sir" was never seen on the highway. At the same time, in the anti-Japanese base camp—the guerrilla team—there was one more person, "Hu Dahai."

Lodging 104

— Su Ying

A moonless night.

Wangjia Village, shrouded in darkness, has no pedestrians on the fields.

Sparse gunshots were ringing in the distance. The dogs in Wangjia Village suddenly barked.

Wang Chunfa's door was ringing like a drum. Wang Chunfa opened the door, and he saw a tall man in short clothes standing outside the door, gasping for breath:

"Sorry, fellow villager! There are devils chasing from the front and back. I am alone, and one tree cannot make a forest. Let me stay for one night, and I will leave at dawn!"

"Um... you..." Wang Chunfa didn't quite understand where he came from.

"I am a New Fourth Army soldier. Tonight, I was ordered to go to Yinjiazhuang over there to suppress the devils. There were twelve of us, and there were more than fifty of them. It's terrible! Eleven of the twelve were lost, and I slipped here alone... Fellow villager! There are devils in front, too. Let me hide for a while, and I will leave at dawn!" He looked east, then west.

The distant gunshots were still ringing sparsely.

"Okay, okay!" Wang Chunfa let the tall man into the house, closed the door, bolted it, and propped it up.

The tall man asked for a towel to wipe his sweat. He groped in his bag and took out a short gun. The gun was empty. He looked at the gun and nodded with a smile:

"Damn it! A full gun of bullets, all eaten by the devils! Hahahaha..."

Wang Chunfa's door was ringing again, even tighter than the tall man had knocked.

Wang Chunfa led the tall man into the pit in the back. Above it was a stinky pigsty. Two fat pigs were not awakened by them and were still snoring soundly.

As soon as Wang Chunfa opened the door, four ferocious yellow-clothed men crowded inside.

They searched the living room, then the kitchen; they rummaged through the bedroom, and stirred up the pigsty, but they couldn't find the tall man. The two fat pigs were disturbed and ran around grunting. With a whistle, they left.

Wang Chunfa closed the door, bolted it, and propped it up.

There was no sound in Wang Chunfa's house, quiet, quiet, quiet until dawn.

The tall man stepped out of Wang Chunfa's door, shook hands with Wang Chunfa, and nodded.

Standing at the Forefront of the Times 105

— Zhou Lihua

Beacon Fire 106

— Zhou Yan

"It's nothing else, we're just too tired. We want to find a girl to comfort us. It's also a way to 'befriend China'!"

Fang Hui took a step back and pointed the × army's box cannon with her finger, saying:

"You say 'befriend', but you point this murderous thing at me. Is this also a way to 'befriend'?"

The × army soldier smiled and was about to hand the box cannon to the person behind him, but Fang Hui quickly stopped him, saying:

"No! The weapon is in your hands. It's the same no matter who you give it to. I will never be fooled. Unless you give it to me, I will believe that you are sincerely 'befriending' us."

The × army soldier was quite hesitant at first, but later, relying on the two guns behind him, and because he was infatuated, he didn't bother to weigh the pros and cons. He actually confidently handed the box cannon to Fang Hui. Fang Hui took the box cannon, smiled, and waved to the × army soldier, saying: "Please come in!"

The × army soldier was overjoyed. The thatched cottage was clearly a city of the unjustly dead, but he mistook it for a comfortable nest. He stretched out his hands, intending to embrace Fang Hui. Fang Hui had already prepared, and gently flicked the mechanism of the box cannon. With a bang, the bullet hit the × army soldier's chest. The × army soldier didn't even have time to shout before he collapsed to the ground. The other two × army soldiers, seeing this change, hurriedly opened fire on Fang Hui. Although the flashlight had already gone out, Fang Hui's left arm was still hit by a bullet. Fortunately, the nurses in the rooms on both sides heard the gunshots and rushed out one after another. Thus, in a fierce fight, the other two × army soldiers were also killed. The small annihilation battle ended victoriously.

Fang Hui had the military doctor in charge dress the wound on her arm, and then, together with the nurses, called out to the villagers. The elderly, weak, women, and children had already heard the gunshots and refused to come out no matter what, until they knew there was no danger. Then, they all gathered tremblingly, and when they saw the bodies of the × army soldiers in front of the thatched cottage, they couldn't help but be surprised. Fang Hui briefly reported the process of killing the enemy just now to them, and said to them:

"If you are obedient subjects under the enemy's hands, you will always be on tenterhooks and will not get a moment's peace. Now that we have done this, the enemy may retaliate against you. I'm thinking for you. The only way is to follow us and join the guerrilla team led by Commander Ye, so that you can save your lives and avoid being harmed by the enemy."

The elderly, weak, women, and children were originally afraid that killing the × army soldiers would implicate them. When they heard Fang Hui say this, they all felt that her words were correct, so they went back to pack their clothes and valuables. Fang Hui also borrowed a pair of door panels from them, piled the bodies of the three × army soldiers on top of them, and, together with the captured spoils of war and the injured warriors who were being treated, were carried by stretcher-bearers and the people, heading north under the starry sky to find Commander Ye's team to rejoin. (3/7)

Shanghai Special Edition

A Brief Account of Shanghai's Charitable Undertakings 107

Huang Hanzhi

According to past history, there were no so-called charitable organizations. Supporting the elderly and caring for children, showing compassion to the lonely and widowed, and burying exposed bones were all matters included in political performance evaluations. Therefore, King Wen's benevolent governance necessarily started with widowers, widows, orphans, and the childless. In later generations, as political teachings gradually declined, members of society, based on their benevolent hearts, provided support and relief to supplement the inadequacies of politics. The so-called "eight hundred lonely and poor" and "ten thousand grand mansions" were purely acts of individual benevolence. Shanghai is a place where people from all directions gather, and the population is dense. In recent years, natural disasters and man-made calamities have been almost constant. In addition, the cost of living is rising daily, and unemployment is increasing. Therefore, charitable undertakings are also being expanded day by day.

During the 16th year of the Republic of China, Mr. Wang Yiting and Hanzhi et al. noted that there were many charitable organizations in the city, and the undertakings they ran were gradually expanding. It was appropriate to have a unified organization to gather wisdom, benefit from diverse perspectives, and unite efforts, so that there would be organized plans internally and substantial strength externally. Hence, the organization of the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Association was established. The undertakings run by each member of the Joint Association are listed below.

Name　Undertaking

Shanghai Charitable Association

Tongren Fuyuan Hall　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing coffins and burial services, running charity schools, sending refugees back home

Renji Shantang　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing coffins, providing relief to widows, running charity schools

Renji Nursery　Nurturing infants

China Jisheng Association　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing relief to widows, providing disaster relief

Xinwei Relief Association　Disaster relief and temporary relief

Lianyi Shanhui　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing coffins, nurturing infants, running charity schools

Guangyi Shantang　Providing medical consultations, distributing clothing and rice, providing relief to widows, providing temporary relief

Pushan Villa　Burial services, hospital

China Relief Association for Women and Children　Sheltering lost and abducted women and children, providing education and care

Hunan Charitable Association　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing relief to widows, running charity schools

China Moral General Association　Educating and caring for orphans, providing relief to women and children, providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, providing coffins

Yimiao Board of Directors　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing clothing and rice, running charity schools

Xinpu Nursery　Establishing a hospital, providing relief to the disabled and orphans, supporting the elderly, nurturing infants

Tongyi Shanhui　Providing medical consultations and medicine, providing coffins, running charity schools

Fushan Tang　Providing medical consultations and medicine, distributing rice, providing relief to widows, running charity schools

Shengde Shanshe　Providing medical consultations and medicine

Huisheng Charitable Society　Providing medical consultations and medicine, running charity schools, releasing animals

Yuanji Tang　Providing medical consultations and medicine, smallpox vaccination

Huili Hospital　Providing medical consultations and medicine

In addition to the above, there are still dozens or hundreds of charitable organizations run by various guilds, associations, and native place associations. The undertakings they run are nothing more than the above-mentioned items. When the August 13th Incident broke out, the addresses of most charitable organizations were in Nanshi and Zhabei, and most of their properties were in Kunshan, Jiading, Songjiang, and Qingpu counties. Some were destroyed by fire, and some were looted. The actual figures for the losses are almost impossible to investigate. Many undertakings were thus suspended. Even those within the concessions were significantly affected, with reduced income and financial difficulties, barely managing to maintain operations. According to a recent written survey by the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Association, the current status of various charitable organizations is as follows.

Name　Current Undertaking　War Losses

Renji Shantang　All operations except schools are running as usual　No income from properties in occupied areas

Houren Tang　Assisting fellow villagers in distress　Most properties were destroyed, impossible to investigate

Weizhong Shantang　Suspended　Slight damage to the hall's foundation

Lianyi Shanhui　Providing coffins, providing medical care　Hall address and nursery were destroyed

Disabled Persons' Home　Sheltering the disabled　Foundation of the home and properties were severely damaged

Pushan Villa　Burial services, providing villages　Properties were almost completely destroyed

China Moral General Association　Barely maintaining original operations　Minor

Zhabei Charitable Association　Suspended　Part of the hall's foundation was destroyed

Zhisheng Shanyuan　Suspended　Properties were almost completely destroyed

Guangyi Shantang　Distributing clothing, providing medicine, providing relief to widows　Properties were severely damaged

China Relief Association for Women and Children　Barely maintaining original operations　Properties were almost completely destroyed

Hunan Charitable Association　Providing temporary medical consultations and medicine　Hall address was not destroyed, but internal losses were significant

Xinwei Relief Association　Providing medicine　None

China Jisheng Association　Six regular charitable activities are barely maintained　Properties had already been completely destroyed during the January 28th Incident

Tongyi Shanhui　Suspended　Hall address was not destroyed, but internal losses were completely destroyed

Gongji Shantang　Suspended　Properties suffered significant losses

Fushan Tang　Suspended　Properties were severely damaged

Zhan Yi Chinese Medicine Hospital　Providing medical consultations and medicine　Properties were severely damaged

Guangye Gongyi Association　Providing coffins, providing medicine　Properties were severely damaged

Other charitable organizations have not yet submitted reports. In short, during this war, the properties of various charitable organizations were almost completely destroyed. It is extremely difficult to seek recovery. Currently, charitable undertakings are focused on providing relief to refugees. A brief account of the refugee relief situation of various relief organizations is as follows.

In the winter of the 25th year, due to the Suiyuan war, charitable organizations throughout the city jointly initiated the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Disaster Relief Association, sending personnel to Suiyuan to distribute emergency relief. The following year, they took over the drought relief in Sichuan, Guizhou, Shaanxi, and Gansu provinces. After the August 13th Incident, the Refugee Relief Committee of the War Zone was established, organizing a monk medical team to rescue wounded soldiers at the front. They established three refugee hospitals and contracted four hospitals, successively rescuing more than 10,000 wounded officers, soldiers, and civilians. They established more than 70 shelters, accommodating more than 200,000 refugees at the peak, and sending more than 50,000 refugees back home. The necessary expenses, in addition to government assistance, were purely dependent on donations from Chinese and foreign philanthropists and enthusiastic overseas Chinese. As of recently, the funds used have reached more than two million yuan. However, in this environment, Shanghai has become an isolated island, with industry and commerce in distress and finance tight. Donations have become exhausted, and the future is uncertain. Therefore, it is necessary to make drastic cuts. Those in charge can only do their best with the people's resources.

At the same time, there was also the Shanghai Branch of the Refugee Relief Association during the Extraordinary Period. After the fall of Shanghai, it was renamed the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Disaster Relief Association Refugee Relief Branch. Chinese and foreign philanthropists formed the Shanghai International Relief Committee. The Chinese Red Cross Society also established an international committee to assist various relief organizations in Shanghai. The committee ended at the end of October. People from all walks of life in China and abroad felt the need for an assistance mechanism of this nature, and the Shanghai Refugee Relief Association was established to take over the tasks of the International Committee and assist various organizations directly accommodating refugees with food and supplies. The approximate number of refugees currently being accommodated by various organizations is as follows.

1. The Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Disaster Relief Association Refugee Relief Committee runs 30 shelters, 4 self-sufficient refugee centers, and 1 vagrant education center, totaling more than 33,300 people.

2. The Refugee Relief Committee Branch of the War Zone runs 40 shelters, with a refugee population of more than 19,700 people.

3. The Shanghai International Relief Committee runs 4 shelters, with a refugee population of more than 10,200 people.

4. The Jiangning Native Place Association and others run 31 shelters, with a refugee population of more than 10,700 people.

5. The Nanshi Refugee Area runs 113 shelters, with a refugee and poor population of more than 41,000 people.

The locations of the above shelters are mostly in the Nanshi Refugee Area. There are 73 shelters in the Public Concession, with more than 53,200 refugees. There are 8 shelters in the French Concession, with more than 15,800 refugees.

As for Tongren Fuyuan Hall and Pushan Villa, since the start of the Shanghai War, they have been entering and leaving the war zone at the risk of their lives to carry out general burial work. Their courageous spirit is especially commendable. The burial grounds are full, and it is difficult to find open spaces within the concessions. The difficulties are even greater. Recently, with the onset of winter, there are fewer deaths. Tongren Fuyuan Hall specializes in burial matters in Nanshi and the French Concession. Pushan Villa specializes in burial matters in the Public Concession, clearly delineating boundaries and working hard. This is also a deformed development.

Shanghai's Traditional Chinese Medicine Industry 108

— Chen Cunren

Shanghai's traditional Chinese medicine industry is quite interesting to discuss. There are 383 traditional Chinese medicine stores and 69 medicinal material stores. Western pharmacies coexist with the traditional Chinese medicine industry, but based on the number of prescriptions dispensed, it can be seen that the foundation of the traditional Chinese medicine industry is long-standing, and the business is flourishing, which is truly surprising and amazing. According to investigations, the daily number of prescriptions dispensed by traditional Chinese medicine stores is: the most is as high as 1,200 prescriptions, 300 prescriptions is the most common, and each store has at least 50 to 60 prescriptions. In total, Shanghai dispenses 70,000 traditional Chinese medicine prescriptions every day. Approximately 58 Chinese-owned Western pharmacies dispense prescriptions, with a total of 3,000 prescriptions dispensed daily. From the perspective of the number of prescriptions dispensed, the ratio is one to twenty-six.

The busiest time for traditional Chinese medicine stores is in the summer, and the most profitable time is in the winter. Recently, medicinal paste prescriptions have become popular. On the full moon day of last month, Hu Qingyu Hall's daily business income reached 24,035 yuan. Other traditional Chinese medicine stores have seen business increase by about 40% due to the concentration of population caused by the war. About 40 new stores have opened this year, and it seems difficult to find stores that will lose money by the end of the year. The usual annual business income reaches more than 9.6 million yuan, which cannot be said to be unsuccessful!

Most traditional Chinese medicine stores have a capital of 20,000 to 30,000 yuan. Tong Hanchun has the largest capital, reaching 1 million taels. Before the war, there were 3,475 employees. Treatment has greatly improved compared to ten years ago. There is a trade association, with my friends Gao Zhiwen, Song Fuchen, Qiu Yanling, Shen Hefu, and Shi Qintang as standing committee members.

Medicinal material stores are divided into firms and numbers: there are 61 medicinal material firms and 8 herbal medicine firms. There are also more than 90 firms from various guilds, divided into mountain goods, northern goods, Sichuan-Han goods, Guangdong goods, and western goods. 35 new stores have opened since the war, some of which were organized by people who were idle after the war, which shows that the business after the war is indeed quite prosperous. The medicinal material firms also formed the Medicinal Material Industry Trade Association, with a very sound organization. My friends Mao Zijian, Fei Tinghua, Dong Bowei, Xia Qizhen, and Chen Wenming are the leaders of the industry. Their command and planning have achieved remarkable results, the recent case being the collection of surcharges from refugees.

In addition to supplying traditional Chinese medicine stores in this and other cities, the medicinal material firms also declare and ship goods to countries around the world. There are no statistics on the annual declarations by medicinal material firms in Shanghai, but it is estimated to be at least more than 3 million yuan. The National Government's Central Pharmaceutical Research Institute recently compiled statistics, stating that the national export of traditional Chinese medicine reached 10 million yuan, which is a surprising gain in the war of resistance economy. Is traditional Chinese medicine useless? Can Chinese people who do not take traditional Chinese medicine not feel ashamed?

The efficacy of traditional Chinese medicine is in line with the physique of the Chinese people, so its business has never declined. The large number of people ordering medicinal paste prescriptions is truly unbelievable to outsiders. On the opening day of Beijing Hongrentang, 60 dan of donkey-hide gelatin were sold. The annual sales of donkey-hide gelatin from Feng Cunren and Cai Tongde are also huge. I believe that if the traditional Chinese medicine industry is improved and guided by new intellectuals to improve the medicines one by one, the results will be far greater than today.

The prepared medicine business of traditional Chinese medicine stores is far less than that of Western medicine. Only Lei Chongshang's Liushen Pills have annual sales of more than 420,000 yuan; Tong Hanchun's Zaizao Pills have annual sales of more than 220,000 yuan; Hu Qingyu's Biwen Pills have annual sales of 100,000 pills; and Tongchuntang's Baibu Paste also has huge sales. Other examples are not easy to point out. In fact, Chinese prepared medicines are very worthy of promotion. Recently, Xia Tieying established the Beijing Pharmacy, because Beijing is the champion of national prepared medicines, hence this specialized organization. Since its opening, the business has been extraordinarily prosperous. The reputation of Beijing medicines has always been good, and the future is very promising. Sanyou Industrial Cooperative has also been paying attention to traditional Chinese medicine in recent years. The daily sales of Zhifeng Pills are 300 boxes, which is not surprising; the daily sales of Fangbian Pills in Shanghai have reached 1,500 bottles, and daily sales in Hong Kong and Southeast Asia have reached 3,000 bottles. This is truly recovering a lot of profits. I believe that if Chinese prepared medicines are promoted using new marketing methods, it will be easier for the business to outperform ordinary Western medicines.

One more point: among the stories of various industries in Shanghai, the traditional Chinese medicine industry has the longest history and the most prosperous business. The Jiang Yanzhe and Yao Taishan stores were recorded in the Shanghai County Chronicles a hundred years ago. At that time, Shanghai was a barren land, and the traditional Chinese medicine business was already impressively visible! This is also a good story.

The most information for this article was provided by Mr. Sun Wenyi, a famous figure in the pharmaceutical industry. Mr. Fei Yongzuo and Mr. Jiang Youcheng of the Pharmaceutical Industry Association also contributed. I express my gratitude in writing.

The Chinese Team and the International Settlement Volunteer Corps 109

— Ming Shihao

Thirty-three Years of Effort and the Growth of the Translation Team

A Brief History of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps: In the 95 years since Shanghai was opened as a port, the International Settlement Volunteer Corps has a long history of 85 years. Although its origins are ancient, its military equipment is quite modern. Although it has been subject to economic difficulties and austerity measures in recent years, it still includes more than 20 teams of different nationalities, including British, American, Chinese, Japanese, Russian, Portuguese, Filipino, and Jewish, and is still a force for emergency relief in the Public Concession.

The establishment of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps in Shanghai dates back to 1853. The motivation for its organization was the influence of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom revolutionary movement. At that time, the concessions did not have the right to station troops for self-defense. Foreign merchants, aware of the booming power of the Hong Yang army and the precarious state of security within the concessions, gathered together with the consuls of various countries in Shanghai to jointly devise defensive measures. They decided to organize volunteer corps from various countries, recruit merchants living in Shanghai to enlist, and appoint Captain Tulangsun, an officer of the British Indian Army, as commander. At that time, American expatriates also formed their own team, commanded by Captain Kyle. This was the beginning of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps. After the Battle of Muddy Creek, it was disbanded for a time. In 1860, the Taiping Army launched a second uprising, and its power was restored. It was re-recruited, and two teams were formed, each with only 80 men. Two years later, under the guidance of Captain Bowlans, it was gradually expanded and began to take shape. In 1870, there were three infantry teams and one light cavalry team, with 200 members. Two mountain guns were transported from Hong Kong, and a field artillery team was established. In 1878, the entire corps was reorganized, the light cavalry team was withdrawn, and two infantry teams were reorganized. At that time, the commander was Mr. Doulitai, and his brother took over his position until Mr. Dou returned to his country in 1882. In 1883, when the entire corps held its first review, there were already 176 officers. Three years later, the artillery team was donated by the British government and obtained four artillery pieces. By 1895, the Portuguese team had joined, and the light cavalry team was also restored. In 1900, after the Boxer Rebellion, the entire corps underwent major changes. At that time, the commander was Major Gracock, and there were 350 members. Later, the Customs team, the American team, the Japanese team, and the armored car team were established and joined one after another, reaching 1,000 people, and the strength was greatly increased. At the same time, the Public Works Department also launched the organization of a machine gun team and purchased many light machine guns, which were distributed to various teams for application. Since then, it has gradually evolved and become more perfect! The powers of the Commander-in-Chief (Corps Commander) have also become more onerous. In the beginning, the corps commanders were all voluntary, but at this point, the Public Works Department requested the British military to send military officers to Shanghai to take charge of the matter, and set a term of three years. The first corps commander was Major Watson, who was succeeded by Captain McGinquan, in 1905, and in 1908 by Major Pence. In 1913, it was Major Whiteley. When the European War broke out, all the soldiers were called back to their countries to participate in the war, and there was no way to send them for a while, so the British military appointed the leader of the corps, Major Truman, as commander to be responsible for the corps affairs. After the war, the old system was restored. The succeeding corps commanders were Major General Manay Johnson in 1920, Colonel Gordon in 1925, Colonel Apun Pamou in 1928, Colonel Slimus in 1931, and Colonel Grehan in 1934. The current corps commander is Colonel Xiang Pei, who took office in 1937. Recently, the average number of people in the entire corps is more than 2,400. Except for about 400 Russian team members who are employed, the rest are volunteer members. The number of people in each team is more than 100, and the number of people in the smaller teams is 40 or 50. The authority to command the International Settlement Volunteer Corps belongs to the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department. The Director-General of the Public Works Department has the responsibility of administrative head of the corps. The highest organization of the corps is the Corps Headquarters, which is divided into the Corps Headquarters Battalion, A Battalion, B Battalion, and C Battalion, and the infantry, cavalry, artillery, armored vehicle, and machine gun teams are all under its command. The order in which the teams joined the International Settlement Volunteer Corps and their names are listed below (in order of the date of formal approval).

Team Name Joining Date

A Team April 1853

B Team 1860

British Light Cavalry Team February 1862

Artillery Team July 1890

Japanese Team July 1900

Armored Car Team December 1903

American Team January 1906

Portuguese Team February 1906

Chinese Team March 1907

Engineering Team June 1909

Scottish Team December 1914

American Light Cavalry Team September 1923

Small Artillery Team September 1924

Russian Team Members January 1927

Russian Team October 1928

Philippine Team February 1932

American Standing Team August 1932

American Machine Gun Team August 1932

Translation Team October 1932

Communications Team August 1932

Transportation Team August 1932

Jewish Team July 1933

A Review of the Chinese Team: Since the opening of Shanghai as a port, there has been no status for Chinese people in international organizations. If there is, it should start with the Volunteer Corps. Because the national power was weak, foreigners discriminated against Chinese people. Therefore, Chinese people did not participate in the International Settlement Volunteer Corps at first. Until 1905, when the Great Trial of the Mixed Court case occurred, the local security was disturbed day and night. Therefore, Chinese business leaders Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Hengzhi, and Hu Jimei believed that the Volunteer Corps maintained local security and protected the lives and property of residents, which was an urgent matter at that time. They then invited more than 100 leaders from various industries to be directors, raised funds to organize, and set up various facilities. It was initially named the Chinese Businessmen's Gymnastics Association, and later renamed the Chinese Team Association. At that time, more than 500 team members were recruited, divided into a military band team, a cavalry team, and four infantry teams, etc., and military uniforms, guns, and equipment were purchased, and training grounds and gyms were established. This was the pioneer of the Chinese Volunteer Corps. Later, the establishment of the Chinese Team was originally closely related to the Chinese people living in the Concession, and since they lived in the Concession, they also had the duty to protect the merchants and people in the Concession. Therefore, they applied to the Public Works Department to join the International Settlement Volunteer Corps as the Chinese Team, and signed an agreement for 83 people to join the team at the Municipal Hall on Nanjing Road in 1907.

The Initial Hard Work: After the agreement was signed, the Corps Commander Watson presented to the Public Works Department to appoint Corbett, the former captain of the Customs Team, as the captain of the Chinese Team, and Grey Lie and Waterc as the deputy captains. Chinese people could only act as platoon leaders with the qualifications of team leaders. However, with the overall team members compromising and striving to improve, and always maintaining a pure combination, they made Chinese and foreign people shift their skeptical views and become enthusiastic admirers, and were treated equally with the teams of various countries. How could we have expected today's prosperity of the Chinese Team!

The Process of Struggle: After the Chinese Team was established, the first time it participated in the overall shooting competition was the "Nevis" trophy in 1909. It was an instant hit, and the results were excellent, which was praised by all sectors at home and abroad. After that, the team competed in the entire corps competition and external competitions, and they were always among the best. To mention the most prominent ones, they won the overall corps competence shield competition more than seven times. It is difficult to describe the victories won in international shooting competitions. It is well known that the Chinese Team's training and shooting are serious and the discipline is strict. All the members of the team can usually be resolute and hardworking, abide by the law and endure hardship. Once they are sent out for defense, they do not hesitate to work hard even in the hot summer and cold winter.

Records of Past Deployments: Since the establishment of the Chinese Team, it has participated in 11 overall corps deployments, including the recovery of Shanghai in 1911, the Second Revolution in 1912, the Third Revolution in 1914, the rickshaw wave and the peddlers' strike in the same year in 1918, the "May Fourth" Movement in 1919, the Jiang-Zhe-Qi-Lu War in 1924, the "May 30th" Massacre in 1925, the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army in 1927, the "January 28th" Sino-Japanese War in 1932, and the recent "August 13th" Anti-Japanese War. In every riot, the Chinese Team was always the first to mobilize and the last to withdraw its defenses. During the deployment period, the tasks of the Chinese Team were no different from those of ordinary troops, either guarding and patrolling to prevent rioters, or providing translators to meet the great needs of emergency situations.

The Origin of the Translation Team: Since the two deployments of "January 28th" and "August 13th", the effectiveness of translators has become more and more obvious. Because the military, police, and Volunteer Corps of various countries gathered in one corner and were frequently mobilized, they were very obstructed by the local dialect. In order to avoid misunderstandings and benefit security, it was urgent to find local help. This is the origin of the Translation Team. In the past, this kind of translator was filled by members of the Chinese Team who were proficient in foreign languages. The organization that formed the group was roughly formed during the "January 28th" Shanghai Incident. At that time, many Chinese employees of various commercial firms who were proficient in Western languages volunteered to serve in the defense lines of various friendly troops and the Volunteer Corps, acting as interpreters for Chinese and foreign soldiers and civilians, eliminating barriers and harmonizing feelings, and achieved good results. However, at that time, it was temporary in nature. Later, Corps Commander Colonel Slimus deeply felt that this organization needed to be established permanently, so he submitted a request to the Public Works Department for approval, and it was officially established as a team of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps on October 1 of that year. The position of team leader was concurrently held by Chen Shixia, the captain of the Chinese Team, who started military training, and Wang Tingkui, Bao Xianqiang, and Zhang Nieyun were appointed as team officers to assist in everything. The team members' uniforms, guns, and training were the same as those of ordinary team members. In recent years, the number of competent team members has often reached 120, and although the team was established not long ago, it has already won the national competent silver shield in the previous session. During the "August 13th" battle last year, the work of the team was particularly valuable, and they were extremely hardworking in their birth and death risks.

Past Team Leaders and Recent Overview: After the establishment of the Chinese Team, in addition to the first two team leaders, the British Mr. Corbett and Mr. Grey Lie, the subsequent successors were Mr. Xu Tonghao (the current corps deputy, who once served as the commander-in-chief of the entire corps), Mr. Hu Yunqiu (the current Chinese affairs consultant of the corps headquarters), Mr. Hao Boyang, Mr. Zhang Tingrong, and Mr. Wang Yanqing. Those who have served as team officers are Mr. Tu Xiantai, Mr. Yang Wenqing, and Mr. Wang Zhiren (the current standing military officer); Chen Shixia, the current captain of the Chinese Team and the Translation Team, took over in the "January 28th" battle; the current team officers of the Chinese Team are Yu Xianen, Li Yushu, Zhou Qingen, and Zhang Tinggui; the team officers of the Translation Team are Wang Yankui, Xu Shaorong, Xia Ranyu, and Zhong Yuting, etc. In recent years, thanks to the effective leadership of the team officers and the efforts of the team members at all levels, the team's performance has become more and more successful, and the number of people has also increased sharply. Recently, there are no less than 600 regular, reserve, and reserve team members. Leading the entire corps and competing for international glory is really commendable. We look forward to the future, how can we limit it? Recently, I heard that the team is starting to recruit new team members for this year. Those with lofty aspirations are willing to return to it.

Spring and Autumn

Job Registration and Talent Scouting 110

— Zhang Lin

The unemployment problem is really serious in Shanghai today. The high statistics have really broken previous records. According to reports, the China Section of the International Labour Office in Geneva has counted 300,000 workers alone. From these figures, we can infer that the overall unemployment figure in Shanghai must be quite high. Although Shanghai has a prosperous appearance at present, what about its internal affairs? The number of employees in the industrial, commercial, agricultural, and academic sectors has not only not increased, but is also decreasing, making it impossible for the general unemployed, especially those with poor knowledge and skills, to find a way out. At the same time, in recent years, thousands of Jews who have suffered unfortunate fates, Japanese who have come to China to "pan for gold," and unemployed White Russians, etc., have come one after another, making the problem of Shanghai's accommodation more and more difficult.

At a time when the tide of unemployment is so turbulent, registering for a job at an employment agency certainly cannot guarantee success, but perhaps there is some hope.

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, affiliated to the Chinese Vocational Education Society, is highly respected by society because of its considerable history and reputation. The work it undertakes to introduce jobs and scout for talents is highly regarded by society. Just step into the door and see the situation in that office where so many unemployed people who are requesting registration gather, and you can know the large number of unemployed people and the arduous work of the institute. Especially in recent years, it has to accept dozens or one or two hundred people for registration and interviews in a few hours of work every day. (No fees are charged)

The first step in registering with the institute is to fill out a job application form. In addition to filling in one's resume in detail, one must also fill in one's expertise, past experience, and spiritual and material hopes in detail, and then fill in the interview registration form and wait for registration and interview in turn.

After the interview, the registrar's appearance, attitude, speech, demeanor, obvious personality, physical characteristics, etc. are recorded one by one, and then this is used as a standard to introduce jobs by chance. However, the number of people who are registered every day who are successfully introduced to jobs is quite low - the reasons for this are naturally multifaceted.

Although there are so many unemployed people in real society, the lack of talent in various departments is quite serious. Many institutions and manufacturers ask the institute to scout for talent on their behalf, but the scope they need is mostly technical talent, such as: engineers, technicians of industrial plants, manufacturing technicians of chemical products, teachers of handicrafts, teachers of specialized subjects in schools, and skilled workers.

After receiving a request, if the registrants do not have such talent, the institute will publicly solicit it in the newspaper. As long as you pay a little attention to the readers of short messages in the local news of major newspapers, you can probably always see it. It is said that various specialized talents are publicly solicited, but they are still not available. It can be seen that there are too few people with knowledge and skills in society. On the contrary, there are too many mediocre people. If we combine the two difficult focal points of any department in real society hoping to obtain sufficient talent and the general mediocre people hoping to obtain good jobs, it is really impossible, except for the popularization of education and the improvement of the economic burden capacity of the general public in studying.

However, we always hope that the general public will learn as much knowledge and skills as possible, and temper their physique. Don't wander around all day because you have no money and no job, and "wait" for a job.

"Old But Vigorous" 111

— Fei Ren

"Respecting the elderly" is a virtue, but respect is only "respect"; it does not mean "praising." But in China, traditionally, "old" is called "longevity." Grand events such as "Centennial Celebrations" are "praised" to the utmost. In fact, human premature death and longevity are very natural phenomena. At most, it makes me learn a little "health care," such as what pharmacies often use the "health care techniques" of "old people" as promotional advertisements.

Yesterday was Mr. Ma Xiangbo's Centennial Celebration, and the Fudan University Alumni Association held a celebration meeting at the New Asia Hotel. "Celebration" naturally also has the meaning of "praising," so is it superfluous? This is exactly the opposite. Mr. Ma Xiangbo's Centennial Celebration should be "praised" and is worth "praising" because what we "praise is not Mr. Ma Xiangbo's centennial," but "praise" Mr. Ma Xiangbo's "spirit."

Although he wrote in a letter to the Fudan University Alumni Association: "Since the war broke out, the country has no peace, the people have no livelihood, and they are displaced in foreign lands. I am ashamed of my lack of virtue and ability, and I always hate longevity and humiliation. I am deeply grateful for your celebration and wishes, and I feel embarrassed." But why did Mr. Ma Xiangbo "displaced in foreign lands"? He is only working hard and running around for the "people" who have "no livelihood" and the "country" that has "no peace." This kind of "spirit" should be and is worth our "praising"! On the contrary, even if you are young and handsome, with a graceful appearance, you are a "decrepit" in "spirit"!

Therefore, "old but vigorous" does not mean that the body is as strong as ever, but that the spirit is as energetic as in youth. On the occasion of Mr. Ma Xiangbo's centennial birthday, I would like to extend my congratulations with these four words, and at the same time encourage myself. We, the young generation, should work harder and make progress!

After the Rain, the Sky Clears 112

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 6: Praising the Longevity of a Person, One Seed Sprouts Three Excellent Talents; Narrating Friendship, Two Scholars Meet Heroes

At this time, He Liyu was very happy and said, "Then the three children are still with you? I must go and see them! I remember when we were in America, it was because of the five girls born in one birth in Morse Town, Canada, that caused a sensation around the world. Not only were visitors flooding through the door, but they also made a fortune in the film industry. There were always several films a year that used these five little sisters to attract audiences. In addition to making films, they were also used for advertising. All kinds of children's medicines and cosmetics used these five little sisters as trademarks. Although we only have two sons in one birth, people have two and a half pairs, and we only have one and a half pairs, which is still one pair short. But I also feel that it is rare. In ancient times, it would be considered a person of longevity." Zhu Ai smiled and said, "If you want to see them, we not only don't refuse, but we also welcome you very much. We take photos of these three little brothers almost every month. We take photos of them from the beginning of their birth at seven days old until now, and we have taken more than ten photos in total. Every time we take a photo, we always remember how many months and days they are. There is a photo album, and their photos are pasted in order. We want to see the process of their development. We will take photos of them again soon, and we also hope that you two and the three of them will take a photo together, which is very meaningful. If you want to see them, you can take you to see them tomorrow, but you can't see them for free, you have to pay a meeting fee!" In the middle of speaking, they were gradually approaching the village where Zhu Ai's hospital was located. It turned out that this town was originally called Anle Town. When the hospital for women and children was first built there, there were not many families in the town, only dozens of families. The hospital was also small in scale, only a church with an attached hospital. Later, through the hard work of that Tong Shengshi, she was a faithful believer who remained chaste and unmarried, and was enthusiastic about saving the world, and many people were moved by her. Her hospital became more and more developed day by day, and the local area became more and more lively day by day. Now the area has also expanded. Counting the gold towns around, there are a total of seven or eight hundred families. Not only that, but there are also several small factories in the town. The neighboring villages and towns are all sericulture farmers. In addition to private sericulture, there are also several collective sericulture places in the town. In addition, there are several weaving factories among the small factories. These sericulture farms and weaving factories are mostly female workers, and they are also most closely related to the women and children's hospital. As for other things such as small schools and libraries, they should have everything. Various facilities such as electric lights and electricity are almost as popular as more prosperous towns. (65)

"Sensations of Going Places" 113

— Li Zhihua

Produced by Warner Bros. Shown at the Grand Theater

It seems that there are too many plays like "Going Places" in Hollywood. I think I should still let the diners reminisce about this kind of play you have seen, - horse racing, music, singing, the so-called "sexy and funny movie", by saying ""The story is like this"".

The "story of" "Going Places" is:

"Young Peter is a clerk of a sports goods company. He is ordered by the owner of the company to impersonate the famous Australian jockey Peter Rendall and carry a large number of sports goods to Marynan for promotion, because the horse racing meeting will be held there soon." As a result, this "impersonating famous jockey" met Colonel Whitling and his wife, who liked to watch horse races, and also met Colonel's son Jack and niece Ellen, a pair of young people who liked to keep horses.

What is even more coincidental is that Jack's beloved horse is named "Gibbs Creebs", who is startled, wild, and unruly, and no one dares to control it; the groom Gabby is good at knowing the horse's intentions, and whenever the horse's wildness breaks out, he always blows a trumpet and plays its special song, and the horse bows its head and obeys, and is unusually docile. And what about that Miss Ellen? Her famous horse "Ellen Girl" is a horse that "has participated in competitions many times and has never won a prize." Now that she sees that Peter's horsemanship is exquisite, she earnestly asks him to help her win the championship.

How is Peter's "exquisite horsemanship" seen? It is: "Gibbs Creebs" was startled and ran out of the stable, and Peter happened to fall on the horse's back: Later, it was thanks to "Gabby who rode a motorcycle and chased after him, and the horse stopped immediately when he heard the music," and the siege was solved.

But it is coincidental that "Ellen Girl" was stolen before the competition, so this "impersonating famous jockey" rode "Gibbs Creebs" to participate in the competition.

This competition also follows the usual practice of Hollywood's "sexy and funny movies." Of course, it must "win the championship," and the hero and heroine meet and End.

"Going Places" is also like this, not an exception at all. As for the way to win, it is "Gabby led a band according to plan and drove a car along the track and played the most favorite songs." However, this time it was not "the horse immediately stopped when it heard the music," this time it was "leading all the way," which was as satisfactory and smooth as the author imagined.

This story is familiar to you: "I seem to have seen it in some movie"? That's what you think, isn't it?

Naturally, your memory is not correct, because "Going Places" is the first time it has been shown in Shanghai; however, it cannot be said that you are wrong, because this kind of film is originally "almost the same."

Then is "Going Places" funny or not? The respectful answer is: I will give you an example, you see if it is funny or not: The groom is good at knowing the horse's intentions, and his trumpet can make the startled horse advance and retreat as he wishes, as the author imagines, he can "stop immediately" with it, and he can also "lead all the way." Do you think this is funny or not?

As for Dick Powell's Peter, he just stood silently on the horse's back, and other than that, he just sang a song with Annie Taylor Louise and others. That song may be used by the band in the dance hall, because there are already many such songs in the dance hall. Isn't it better and more fresh to have one more song?

The Life of a Female Office Worker (Continued) 114

— Tsunami

Therefore, to apply for a female office worker position, one must have a standard "marketable appearance." Otherwise, even if you speak perfect "Yes, All-right" like a foreigner, it would still be difficult to pass the examination.

Although there are no strict regulations regarding qualifications for application, one must at least have an education level of having attended or graduated from middle school. Great importance is placed on conversational English, as well as proficiency in various domestic dialects. For example, Cantonese and Northern Mandarin are highly welcomed by the bosses. Next in importance is proficiency in abacus calculation, which is also a key part of the examination. As for Chinese language proficiency, it seems to be of the least importance. As long as you can write simple memos, you don't have to worry about failing the exam.

Speaking of female office workers' salaries, there's a great disparity even for the same position. Monthly pay ranges from seven or eight yuan to a maximum of twenty-plus yuan. How could that little money be enough? Just their expenses on makeup are quite considerable! Therefore, many female office workers need their families, like their fathers and brothers, to supplement their income, in addition to what they earn themselves. Clearly, a female office worker's fashionable attire is a case of "a poor man putting on airs," simply maintaining appearances!

Now let me talk about the extracurricular life of female office workers. A person's life is easily influenced by the surrounding environment. Those who can control the environment are the most rational and the most resolute. Often, innocent and pure girls, fresh out of school, enter these extravagant and decadent environments, and their eyes and ears are influenced, leading to transformation. Those who didn't perm their hair before start to perm it like everyone else. Those who used to find people wearing high heels strange and repulsive now wear them as a matter of course. Those who used to care about national affairs now find even reading a newspaper uninteresting. Generally speaking, female office workers are considered intellectuals, but in reality, out of a hundred female office workers, perhaps only ten or so read the newspaper every day. This is not the author intentionally exaggerating to sensationalize but rather facts seen and heard! Perhaps some alert female office workers share the same sentiments.

Speaking of their general leisure activities, under the guidance of some male colleagues, many frequently go to cinemas and theaters. Naturally, their main purpose is to use the cinema to live a life of "pseudo-romance." However, most female office workers spend their leisure time at home, helping their parents with trivial household chores or leading a muddled and unconscious private family life.

Of course, we cannot deny that a small number of female office workers have awakened amidst the sound of the Anti-Japanese War. They are participating in various direct and indirect anti-Japanese efforts. In the midst of a luxurious environment, they strengthen their resolve and actively carry out the sacred task of awakening and organizing their generally unfocused female colleagues, which is the fundamental work for the women's liberation movement. These dedicated and hardworking female warriors are worthy of our praise. (The End)
